Choose a specific brownfield redevelopment project and analyze its impact on public health. What strategies were used to mitigate potential health risks? Were there any challenges or successes in addressing public health concerns?



#### Exercise 5: Future Considerations

Consider the future of brownfield redevelopment and its potential impact on public health. How can we continue to improve and prioritize public health in these projects? What role can environmental and public health professionals play in shaping the future of brownfield redevelopment?





## Chapter: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Introduction:



Brownfield redevelopment is the process of revitalizing and reusing contaminated or abandoned properties for new development. These properties, known as brownfields, often have a negative impact on the surrounding environment and community. However, with proper management and remediation, brownfields can be transformed into valuable assets for economic development.



In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and economic development. We will discuss the challenges and opportunities associated with redeveloping brownfields, as well as the various stakeholders involved in the process. Additionally, we will examine the economic benefits of brownfield redevelopment, including job creation, increased property values, and improved community well-being.



Through case studies and real-world examples, we will highlight successful brownfield redevelopment projects and the strategies used to achieve them. We will also address the potential environmental and social impacts of brownfield redevelopment and the importance of sustainable practices in the process.



Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of brownfield redevelopment and its role in promoting economic development. By the end, readers will have a deeper appreciation for the potential of brownfields and the importance of responsible environmental management in achieving successful redevelopment.





# Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



## Chapter 11: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Section 11.1: Economic Impacts of Brownfields



Brownfield redevelopment is a complex process that involves the remediation and revitalization of contaminated or abandoned properties for new development. This process has significant economic impacts, both positive and negative, on the surrounding community and the overall economy. In this section, we will explore the various economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment and their implications.



#### 11.1a: Overview of Economic Impacts



The economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment can be categorized into positive and negative impacts. Positive impacts include job creation, increased property values, and improved community well-being. On the other hand, negative impacts may include increased electricity prices and potential regressive effects on low-income households.



One of the most significant positive impacts of brownfield redevelopment is job creation. The process of remediation and redevelopment requires a significant amount of labor, which can lead to the creation of new jobs in the local community. Additionally, once the brownfield is redeveloped, it can attract new businesses and industries, further contributing to job growth.



Another positive impact of brownfield redevelopment is the increase in property values. By revitalizing a contaminated or abandoned property, the surrounding area becomes more desirable for development and can lead to an increase in property values. This can benefit both property owners and the local government through increased tax revenue.



Furthermore, brownfield redevelopment can also have a positive impact on community well-being. By transforming a blighted area into a vibrant and productive space, the community can experience improved quality of life and a sense of pride in their neighborhood.



However, there are also potential negative impacts and trade-offs associated with brownfield redevelopment. One of the main concerns is the potential increase in electricity prices. The process of remediation and redevelopment can be energy-intensive, leading to higher electricity costs for the developer and potentially for the surrounding community.



Moreover, studies have shown that in the absence of social benefits and tax credits, brownfield redevelopment may have regressive effects on low-income households. This is because the costs of remediation and redevelopment may be passed on to consumers, leading to higher prices for goods and services.



In addition to these impacts, economic impact analyses often estimate the sources of the impacts. These can include direct effects, such as the initial money spent on salaries and supplies, as well as indirect and induced effects, which refer to the ripple effects of the initial spending on the local economy.



In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment has significant economic impacts, both positive and negative, on the surrounding community and the overall economy. It is essential for stakeholders to carefully consider these impacts and trade-offs when embarking on a brownfield redevelopment project. By understanding the economic implications, we can ensure that brownfield redevelopment is a sustainable and beneficial process for all involved.





# Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



## Chapter 11: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Section 11.1: Economic Impacts of Brownfields



Brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in recent years as communities across the United States seek to revitalize contaminated or abandoned properties for new development. This process has significant economic impacts, both positive and negative, on the surrounding community and the overall economy. In this section, we will explore the various economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment and their implications.



#### 11.1a: Overview of Economic Impacts



The economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment can be categorized into positive and negative impacts. Positive impacts include job creation, increased property values, and improved community well-being. On the other hand, negative impacts may include increased electricity prices and potential regressive effects on low-income households.



One of the most significant positive impacts of brownfield redevelopment is job creation. The process of remediation and redevelopment requires a significant amount of labor, which can lead to the creation of new jobs in the local community. This not only benefits the individuals who are employed, but also has a ripple effect on the local economy as these workers spend their income on goods and services in the community.



Another positive impact of brownfield redevelopment is the increase in property values. By revitalizing a contaminated or abandoned property, the surrounding area becomes more desirable for development and can lead to an increase in property values. This can benefit both property owners and the local government through increased tax revenue. Additionally, as property values increase, it can attract new businesses and industries to the area, further contributing to economic growth.



Furthermore, brownfield redevelopment can also have a positive impact on community well-being. By transforming a blighted area into a vibrant and productive space, the community can experience improved quality of life and a sense of pride in their neighborhood. This can lead to increased community involvement and a stronger sense of community identity.



However, there are also potential negative impacts of brownfield redevelopment that must be considered. One of these is the potential for increased electricity prices. As brownfield sites are often contaminated with hazardous materials, the remediation process can be energy-intensive and may lead to increased electricity costs for the community. This can have a regressive effect on low-income households who may struggle to afford these increased costs.



In addition, there may be concerns about the displacement of low-income residents as a result of brownfield redevelopment. As property values increase and new businesses move into the area, there is a risk that low-income residents may be forced to relocate due to rising housing costs. This can have a negative impact on the community and may lead to gentrification.



To address these potential negative impacts, it is important for communities to carefully consider the economic implications of brownfield redevelopment and develop strategies to mitigate any negative effects. This may include providing affordable housing options, implementing energy-efficient practices during the remediation process, and involving the local community in the decision-making process.



In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment has significant economic impacts on both the local community and the overall economy. While there are potential negative impacts, the positive effects, such as job creation and increased property values, can greatly benefit a community. By carefully considering and addressing these impacts, brownfield redevelopment can be a valuable tool for economic development and revitalization.





# Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



## Chapter 11: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Section 11.1: Economic Impacts of Brownfields



Brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in recent years as communities across the United States seek to revitalize contaminated or abandoned properties for new development. This process has significant economic impacts, both positive and negative, on the surrounding community and the overall economy. In this section, we will explore the various economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment and their implications.



#### 11.1a: Overview of Economic Impacts



The economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment can be categorized into positive and negative impacts. Positive impacts include job creation, increased property values, and improved community well-being. On the other hand, negative impacts may include increased electricity prices and potential regressive effects on low-income households.



One of the most significant positive impacts of brownfield redevelopment is job creation. The process of remediation and redevelopment requires a significant amount of labor, which can lead to the creation of new jobs in the local community. This not only benefits the individuals who are employed, but also has a ripple effect on the local economy as these workers spend their income on goods and services in the community.



Another positive impact of brownfield redevelopment is the increase in property values. By revitalizing a contaminated or abandoned property, the surrounding area becomes more desirable for development and can lead to an increase in property values. This can benefit both property owners and the local government through increased tax revenue. Additionally, as property values increase, it can attract new businesses and industries to the area, further contributing to economic growth.



Furthermore, brownfield redevelopment can also have a positive impact on community well-being. By cleaning up and redeveloping contaminated sites, the overall health and safety of the community can be improved. This can lead to a better quality of life for residents and attract new residents to the area.



On the other hand, there are also potential negative impacts of brownfield redevelopment. One of these is the potential for increased electricity prices. The process of remediation and redevelopment can be energy-intensive, leading to higher electricity costs for the community. This can have a disproportionate impact on low-income households, potentially leading to regressive effects.



#### 11.1b: Case Studies in Economic Development and Brownfield Redevelopment



To better understand the economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment, let's examine some case studies of successful projects. One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel plant in Bethlehem, Pennsylvania. This site was contaminated with heavy metals and other pollutants from its previous use as a steel manufacturing plant. However, through a partnership between the local government, private developers, and community organizations, the site was cleaned up and redeveloped into a mixed-use development with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This project not only created jobs and increased property values, but also revitalized the surrounding community and improved the overall economic health of the area.



Another successful case study is the redevelopment of the former Stapleton Airport in Denver, Colorado. This site was contaminated with petroleum and other hazardous substances from its previous use as an airport. However, through a public-private partnership, the site was cleaned up and redeveloped into a sustainable community with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This project not only created jobs and increased property values, but also improved the overall environmental sustainability of the area.



#### 11.1c: Economic Benefits of Brownfield Redevelopment



In addition to the direct economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment, there are also indirect economic benefits that should be considered. These include cost savings for construction companies and building owners, as well as the environmental benefits of repurposing existing buildings and materials rather than constructing new ones. By repurposing existing buildings, the cost of producing new materials and the associated services is reduced, leading to cost savings for all parties involved. Additionally, repurposing materials reduces waste and the environmental impact of new construction.



In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment has significant economic impacts, both positive and negative, on the surrounding community and the overall economy. By understanding these impacts and considering them in the planning and implementation of redevelopment projects, we can ensure that brownfield redevelopment is not only environmentally sustainable, but also economically beneficial for all stakeholders involved. 





# Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



## Chapter 11: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies



#### 11.2a Overview of Economic Development Strategies



In order to understand the economic impacts of brownfield redevelopment, it is important to first understand the different strategies that have been used in economic development. Economic development research has identified five phases, or "waves," of economic development practice. These waves have been shaped by historical factors, economic climates, and leaders' responses to these forces, resulting in five distinct strategies that differ from their predecessors.



The first wave of economic development, known as the Growth Promotion Approach, emerged in the United States in the 1930s as a response to the Great Depression. This approach focused on industrial recruitment through financial incentives such as tax abatement and loans. The goal was to lower costs associated with land, infrastructure, and labor in order to attract businesses and stimulate economic growth. This method of business attraction became known as "smokestack-chasing."



Smokestack-chasing is rooted in the "boosterism" of small towns in early North America. In this wave, economic developers focused on attracting one major employer to the region, whether it be a factory, mine, college, or prison. The first step in smokestack-chasing was to promote the location to potential employers. Then, economic developers would provide incentives, such as cheap land or labor and lax environmental regulations, to improve the likelihood of the employer locating within the area.



However, this approach to economic development has been criticized for being haphazard and ineffective. Detractors argue that smokestack-chasing may lead to short-term job growth, but the long-term effects are often mixed. Additionally, this strategy has been accused of neglecting the potential negative impacts on the environment and surrounding community.



Despite its criticisms, smokestack-chasing remains a prevalent strategy in economic development, often operating concurrently with other waves. As we will explore in the next section, brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in economic development, and it is often seen as a more sustainable and responsible approach to revitalizing communities and promoting economic growth.





# Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



## Chapter 11: Brownfield Redevelopment and Economic Development



### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies



#### 11.2b Selection of Economic Development Strategies



In order to effectively redevelop brownfield sites, it is important to understand and select appropriate economic development strategies. As mentioned in the previous section, there have been five distinct waves of economic development practice, each with its own set of strategies. In this section, we will discuss the selection of economic development strategies and how they can be applied to brownfield redevelopment.



The first step in selecting economic development strategies is to assess the current economic climate and the specific needs and challenges of the community. This can be done through a thorough analysis of the local economy, including industries, employment rates, and income levels. It is also important to consider the potential impacts of brownfield redevelopment on the community, such as job creation, tax revenue, and environmental benefits.



Once the economic climate and community needs have been assessed, economic developers can then consider which strategies would be most effective in achieving their goals. One strategy that has been successful in brownfield redevelopment is the Growth Management Approach. This approach focuses on promoting sustainable economic growth by investing in existing businesses and industries, rather than solely relying on attracting new businesses. This can be achieved through initiatives such as workforce development programs, infrastructure improvements, and business retention and expansion programs.



Another strategy that has been effective in brownfield redevelopment is the Cluster Development Approach. This approach focuses on developing and supporting clusters of related industries in a specific region. By promoting collaboration and knowledge sharing among businesses in the same industry, this approach can lead to increased innovation and competitiveness. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, this strategy can be applied by targeting industries that have a high demand for remediation services, such as manufacturing or transportation.



In addition to these strategies, economic developers may also consider the use of incentives to attract businesses to redevelop brownfield sites. These incentives can include tax breaks, grants, and low-interest loans. However, it is important to carefully consider the potential long-term impacts of these incentives, as they may not always lead to sustainable economic growth.



Ultimately, the selection of economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment should be based on a thorough understanding of the local economy and community needs. By carefully considering the potential impacts and benefits of each strategy, economic developers can effectively promote sustainable economic growth while also addressing the environmental challenges of brownfield sites.





### Section: 11.2 Economic Development Strategies



#### 11.2c Case Studies in Economic Development Strategies



In addition to understanding and selecting appropriate economic development strategies, it is important to examine case studies of successful brownfield redevelopment projects. These case studies can provide valuable insights and lessons learned for future projects.



One such case study is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Bethlehem, Pennsylvania. This site was once a thriving steel mill, but after its closure in 1995, it became a brownfield site with significant environmental contamination. The redevelopment project, led by the Bethlehem Redevelopment Authority, focused on creating a mixed-use development that would bring economic growth and job opportunities to the community.



The project utilized a combination of economic development strategies, including the Growth Management Approach and the Cluster Development Approach. The site was divided into different zones, with a mix of residential, commercial, and industrial uses. This allowed for the creation of a diverse and sustainable economy, with a focus on retaining and expanding existing businesses in the area.



The project also incorporated environmental remediation efforts, including the removal of contaminated soil and the installation of a groundwater treatment system. This not only improved the environmental quality of the site, but also made it more attractive to potential businesses and residents.



The success of the Bethlehem Steel redevelopment project can be seen in the economic impact it has had on the community. The site now houses over 2,000 employees and generates over $1 billion in economic activity annually. It has also become a hub for innovation and entrepreneurship, with the development of a business incubator and a technology center.



Another successful case study is the redevelopment of the former Ford Motor Company plant in St. Paul, Minnesota. This site was also contaminated and had been vacant for over a decade before being redeveloped. The project, led by the St. Paul Port Authority, focused on creating a sustainable and environmentally-friendly industrial park.



The project utilized a combination of economic development strategies, including the Growth Management Approach and the Sustainable Development Approach. The site was designed to be energy-efficient and incorporate green infrastructure, such as rain gardens and permeable pavement. This not only reduced the environmental impact of the site, but also attracted businesses that were committed to sustainability.



The redevelopment of the Ford Motor Company plant has had a significant economic impact on the community. The site now houses over 2,000 employees and generates over $100 million in annual economic activity. It has also become a model for sustainable industrial development, with other cities looking to replicate its success.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of understanding and selecting appropriate economic development strategies for brownfield redevelopment. They also highlight the potential for economic growth and job creation in communities that have been impacted by brownfield sites. By utilizing a combination of strategies and incorporating environmental remediation efforts, brownfield redevelopment projects can not only revitalize communities, but also create a more sustainable and resilient economy.





### Section: 11.3 Economic Development and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of economic development initiatives, particularly in the context of brownfield redevelopment. As discussed in the previous section, community economic development (CED) emphasizes the active involvement of community members in all aspects of development that affect their standard of living. This approach is especially relevant in the case of brownfield redevelopment, as these projects often have a direct impact on the surrounding community.



One of the key benefits of community engagement in economic development is the promotion of local resources and opportunities. By involving community members in the decision-making process, CED initiatives can identify and utilize local resources in a way that benefits both the community and the economy. This can include the creation of new jobs, the development of local businesses, and the improvement of social conditions.



In addition, community engagement can help to address and overcome crises and challenges faced by disadvantaged communities. By actively involving community members in the planning and implementation of economic development strategies, CED initiatives can better understand and address the specific needs and concerns of the community. This can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions that benefit both the economy and the community.



Furthermore, community engagement can contribute to the capacity building of stakeholders involved in economic development. This includes not only community members, but also governments, businesses, and non-profit organizations. By promoting collaboration and participation, CED initiatives can increase the ability and desire of these stakeholders to effectively engage in economic development. This can lead to more successful and sustainable projects in the long run.



A notable example of the role of community engagement in economic development can be seen in the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Bethlehem, Pennsylvania. As discussed in the previous section, this project utilized a combination of economic development strategies to create a mixed-use development that would bring economic growth and job opportunities to the community. However, the success of this project can also be attributed to the active involvement of community members in the decision-making process. This not only ensured that the project addressed the specific needs and concerns of the community, but also fostered a sense of ownership and pride in the development.



In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial component of economic development, particularly in the context of brownfield redevelopment. By actively involving community members in the planning and implementation of economic development strategies, CED initiatives can promote the use of local resources, address community challenges, and contribute to the capacity building of stakeholders. This ultimately leads to more successful and sustainable economic development projects that benefit both the economy and the community.





### Section: 11.3 Economic Development and Community Engagement:

As discussed in the previous section, community economic development (CED) emphasizes the active involvement of community members in all aspects of development that affect their standard of living. This approach is especially relevant in the case of brownfield redevelopment, as these projects often have a direct impact on the surrounding community.

This can include the creation of new jobs, the development of local businesses, and the improvement of social conditions.

This can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions that benefit both the economy and the community.

This includes not only community members, but also governments, businesses, and non-profit organizations. By promoting collaboration and participation, CED initiatives can increase the ability and desire of these stakeholders to effectively engage in economic development. This can lead to more successful and sustainable projects in the long run.



A notable example of the role of community engagement in economic development can be seen in the Workforce Innovation in Regional Economic Development (WIRED) initiative. This program, funded by the U.S. federal government, focuses on regional growth and emphasizes the importance of human capital and "soft" infrastructure in economic development. One of the key components of WIRED is community engagement, which allows for the identification and utilization of local resources and the addressing of specific needs and concerns of the community.



In order to effectively engage the community in economic development, there are various techniques that can be utilized. These include:



#### 11.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Economic Development:



1. Community meetings and forums: These provide a platform for community members to voice their opinions and concerns, and for stakeholders to gather feedback and ideas from the community.



2. Surveys and questionnaires: These can be used to gather data and opinions from a larger sample of the community, providing a more comprehensive understanding of their needs and preferences.



3. Focus groups: These involve a small group of community members who are brought together to discuss specific topics related to economic development. This allows for more in-depth discussions and the gathering of diverse perspectives.



4. Community outreach and education: This involves actively reaching out to community members and educating them about the economic development project and its potential benefits. This can help to build trust and support from the community.



5. Collaborative planning and decision-making: By involving community members in the planning and decision-making process, stakeholders can ensure that the project aligns with the needs and priorities of the community.



Overall, these techniques can help to foster a sense of ownership and involvement among community members, leading to more successful and sustainable economic development initiatives.

A notable example of the role of community engagement in economic development can be seen in the Workforce Innovation in Regional Economic Development (WIRED) initiative. This program, funded by the U.S. federal government, focuses on promoting regional growth through the active involvement of community members, governments, and businesses. By incorporating well-accepted economic development practices and promoting collaboration among stakeholders, WIRED has been successful in stimulating innovation and technology spillover in grantee regions.



Another example is the Think Resilience online course, developed by university research labs, which focuses on building resilience in communities through economic development. This course highlights the importance of community engagement in addressing and overcoming challenges faced by disadvantaged communities.



In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial aspect of economic development, particularly in the context of brownfield redevelopment. ### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the important relationship between brownfield redevelopment and economic development. We have seen how the revitalization of contaminated sites can bring about numerous economic benefits, such as job creation, increased property values, and improved community health. We have also discussed the various challenges and barriers that may arise during the brownfield redevelopment process, and how these can be overcome through effective environmental management practices.



Through the case studies and examples presented in this chapter, it is clear that brownfield redevelopment can be a powerful tool for promoting sustainable economic growth. By repurposing underutilized or contaminated land, we can not only improve the environment, but also create new opportunities for businesses and communities. However, it is important to note that successful brownfield redevelopment requires collaboration and cooperation among various stakeholders, including government agencies, private developers, and local communities.



As we move towards a more sustainable future, it is crucial that we continue to prioritize brownfield redevelopment as a key component of environmental management. By incorporating economic development into our environmental strategies, we can create a win-win situation for both the environment and the economy. It is our hope that this chapter has provided valuable insights and practical guidance for those involved in brownfield redevelopment projects.

#### Exercise 2: Cost-Benefit Analysis

Choose a brownfield redevelopment project and conduct a cost-benefit analysis. Consider the economic benefits, environmental benefits, and potential costs associated with the project. Discuss the overall feasibility and potential impact of the project.

#### Exercise 5: Sustainable Development Goals

Choose one of the United Nations' Sustainable Development Goals and discuss how brownfield redevelopment can contribute to achieving this goal. Consider the economic, social, and environmental aspects of the goal and how brownfield redevelopment can address them.





## Chapter: Brownfield Redevelopment and Social Equity



### Introduction:



In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of brownfield redevelopment and its relationship with social equity. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that are potentially contaminated with hazardous substances. These properties often pose a threat to public health and the environment, and their redevelopment can have significant impacts on the surrounding community. 



The concept of social equity refers to the fair distribution of resources and opportunities among all members of a society. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, social equity is concerned with ensuring that the benefits and burdens of the redevelopment process are distributed fairly among all stakeholders, particularly those who have historically been marginalized or disadvantaged. 



In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and social equity, and discuss the challenges and opportunities that arise in this context. We will also examine the role of environmental management practitioners in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of the importance of considering social equity in brownfield redevelopment and the strategies that can be employed to achieve it.





### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has significant social impacts on the surrounding community. These impacts can be both positive and negative, and it is important for environmental management practitioners to consider them in order to promote social equity in the redevelopment process.



#### 12.1a Overview of Social Impacts



The redevelopment of brownfields can have a range of social impacts, including changes in socioeconomics, quality of life, and poverty rates. These impacts are often interconnected and can have a domino effect on the community.



One of the most significant social impacts of brownfield redevelopment is on socioeconomics. The process of redeveloping a brownfield can bring new economic opportunities to the community, such as job creation and increased tax revenue. However, it can also lead to gentrification and displacement of low-income residents. This can create a divide between those who benefit from the redevelopment and those who are negatively impacted by it.



The quality of life in the surrounding community can also be affected by brownfield redevelopment. Studies have shown that access to social services, such as healthcare and education, can have a positive impact on quality of life. Therefore, the redevelopment of brownfields should also consider the provision of these services to the community.



Additionally, brownfield redevelopment can have an impact on poverty rates. The inclusion of welfare programs as part of social services can help alleviate poverty in the community. However, if these programs are not properly implemented, they may not reach those who need them the most, leading to continued poverty and inequality.



In order to promote social equity in brownfield redevelopment, it is important for environmental management practitioners to consider these social impacts and work towards mitigating any negative effects. This can be achieved through community engagement and collaboration with stakeholders to ensure that the benefits and burdens of the redevelopment are distributed fairly. Additionally, incorporating social impact assessments into the redevelopment process can help identify potential issues and inform decision-making.



In conclusion, the redevelopment of brownfields has significant social impacts on the surrounding community. It is crucial for environmental management practitioners to consider these impacts and work towards promoting social equity in the redevelopment process. By doing so, we can ensure that the benefits of brownfield redevelopment are shared by all members of the community, regardless of their socioeconomic status.





### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has significant social impacts on the surrounding community. These impacts can be both positive and negative, and it is important for environmental management practitioners to consider them in order to promote social equity in the redevelopment process.



#### 12.1a Overview of Social Impacts



The redevelopment of brownfields can have a range of social impacts, including changes in socioeconomics, quality of life, and poverty rates. These impacts are often interconnected and can have a domino effect on the community.



One of the most significant social impacts of brownfield redevelopment is on socioeconomics. The process of redeveloping a brownfield can bring new economic opportunities to the community, such as job creation and increased tax revenue. However, it can also lead to gentrification and displacement of low-income residents. This can create a divide between those who benefit from the redevelopment and those who are negatively impacted by it. To address this issue, environmental management practitioners should prioritize community engagement and collaboration with local organizations to ensure that the needs and concerns of all community members are taken into account during the redevelopment process. This can help to promote social equity and prevent the displacement of vulnerable populations.



The quality of life in the surrounding community can also be affected by brownfield redevelopment. Studies have shown that access to social services, such as healthcare and education, can have a positive impact on quality of life. Therefore, the redevelopment of brownfields should also consider the provision of these services to the community. This can be achieved through partnerships with local healthcare providers and educational institutions, as well as the implementation of programs that provide access to these services for community members.



Additionally, brownfield redevelopment can have an impact on poverty rates. The inclusion of welfare programs as part of social services can help alleviate poverty in the community. However, if these programs are not properly implemented, they may not reach those who need them the most, leading to continued poverty and inequality. Environmental management practitioners should work closely with local government agencies and community organizations to ensure that these programs are effectively implemented and reach those who are most in need.



In conclusion, social equity should be a key consideration in brownfield redevelopment. Environmental management practitioners have a responsibility to address the social impacts of brownfields and work towards promoting social equity in the communities where redevelopment takes place. This can be achieved through community engagement, collaboration with local organizations, and the implementation of programs and services that benefit all members of the community. 





### Section: 12.1 Social Impacts of Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has significant social impacts on the surrounding community. These impacts can be both positive and negative, and it is important for environmental management practitioners to consider them in order to promote social equity in the redevelopment process.



#### 12.1a Overview of Social Impacts



The redevelopment of brownfields can have a range of social impacts, including changes in socioeconomics, quality of life, and poverty rates. These impacts are often interconnected and can have a domino effect on the community.



One of the most significant social impacts of brownfield redevelopment is on socioeconomics. The process of redeveloping a brownfield can bring new economic opportunities to the community, such as job creation and increased tax revenue. However, it can also lead to gentrification and displacement of low-income residents. This can create a divide between those who benefit from the redevelopment and those who are negatively impacted by it. To address this issue, environmental management practitioners should prioritize community engagement and collaboration with local organizations to ensure that the needs and concerns of all community members are taken into account during the redevelopment process. This can help to promote social equity and prevent the displacement of vulnerable populations.



The quality of life in the surrounding community can also be affected by brownfield redevelopment. Studies have shown that access to social services, such as healthcare and education, can have a positive impact on quality of life. Therefore, the redevelopment of brownfields should also consider the provision of these services to the community. This can be achieved through partnerships with local healthcare providers and educational institutions, as well as the implementation of programs that provide access to these services for community members.



Additionally, brownfield redevelopment can have a significant impact on poverty rates in the surrounding community. By creating new economic opportunities and improving the quality of life, brownfield redevelopment can help to reduce poverty rates. However, it is important for environmental management practitioners to consider the potential negative impacts on low-income residents and work to mitigate them through community engagement and collaboration.



#### 12.1b Social Equity in Brownfield Redevelopment



Social equity is a key consideration in the redevelopment of brownfields. It refers to the fair distribution of benefits and burdens among all members of a community. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, social equity means ensuring that all community members, regardless of their socioeconomic status, have equal access to the benefits of the redevelopment process.



One way to promote social equity in brownfield redevelopment is through community engagement and collaboration. This involves actively involving community members in the decision-making process and considering their needs and concerns. By working closely with local organizations and residents, environmental management practitioners can ensure that the redevelopment process is inclusive and benefits all members of the community.



Another important aspect of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment is through the provision of affordable housing. As mentioned earlier, gentrification can lead to the displacement of low-income residents. To prevent this, affordable housing should be incorporated into the redevelopment plan. This can be achieved through partnerships with affordable housing organizations and the implementation of policies that require a certain percentage of housing units to be affordable for low-income residents.



#### 12.1c Case Studies in Social Equity and Brownfield Redevelopment



To further illustrate the importance of social equity in brownfield redevelopment, let us look at two case studies: Discovery Green in Houston, Texas and the Voluntary Cleanup Program in Texas.



##### Discovery Green



In 2004, a public-private partnership was formed to create the Discovery Green Conservancy in downtown Houston, Texas. This partnership involved the Brown Foundation, the Kinder Foundation, the Wortham Foundation, the Houston Endowment, Inc., and the City of Houston. The goal was to transform an undeveloped and underused parking lot with a history of industrial occupants into a downtown city park.



One of the key aspects of this project was the focus on social equity. The Discovery Green Conservancy worked closely with local organizations and residents to ensure that the park would benefit all members of the community. This included providing access to social services, such as healthcare and education, and incorporating affordable housing into the redevelopment plan. As a result, Discovery Green has become a popular and inclusive public space that promotes social equity in the surrounding community.



##### Voluntary Cleanup Program in Texas



In Texas, the Texas Commission on Environmental Quality (TCEQ) has a Voluntary Cleanup Program (VCP) that provides incentives for the investigation, cleanup, and redevelopment of brownfields. This program has been successful in promoting social equity by actively involving community members in the redevelopment process and prioritizing the needs and concerns of all residents.



Through the VCP, the TCEQ works closely with local organizations and residents to ensure that the redevelopment of brownfields benefits the community as a whole. This includes providing access to social services and incorporating affordable housing into the redevelopment plan. By promoting social equity, the VCP has successfully revitalized numerous brownfield sites while also benefiting the surrounding community.



#### Conclusion



In conclusion, social equity is a crucial consideration in the redevelopment of brownfields. By actively involving community members in the decision-making process and prioritizing their needs and concerns, environmental management practitioners can promote social equity and prevent the displacement of vulnerable populations. Through partnerships with local organizations and the provision of affordable housing and social services, brownfield redevelopment can have a positive impact on the surrounding community and promote social equity. 





### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:



#### 12.2a Overview of Social Equity Strategies



Social equity is a critical aspect of brownfield redevelopment that must be carefully considered by environmental management practitioners. It refers to the fair distribution of resources, opportunities, and benefits among all members of a community, regardless of their race, ethnicity, income, or other social factors. In this section, we will discuss some strategies that can promote social equity in the brownfield redevelopment process.



One of the key strategies for promoting social equity is community engagement. This involves actively involving community members in the decision-making process and considering their needs and concerns. Environmental management practitioners should collaborate with local organizations and community leaders to ensure that the redevelopment plans align with the community's goals and priorities. This can help to prevent the displacement of vulnerable populations and promote a sense of ownership and inclusivity within the community.



Another important strategy is the provision of affordable housing. As mentioned earlier, brownfield redevelopment can lead to gentrification and displacement of low-income residents. To address this issue, environmental management practitioners should work with developers to incorporate affordable housing units into the redevelopment plans. This can help to maintain the diversity and social fabric of the community and prevent the exclusion of marginalized populations.



In addition to affordable housing, access to social services is also crucial for promoting social equity. As the quality of life in the surrounding community can be affected by brownfield redevelopment, it is important to consider the provision of healthcare, education, and other essential services. This can be achieved through partnerships with local service providers and the implementation of programs that provide access to these services for community members.



Furthermore, environmental management practitioners should also prioritize job creation and training programs for local residents. This can help to address the issue of unemployment and promote economic opportunities for community members. Additionally, it is important to ensure that these job opportunities are accessible to all members of the community, regardless of their background or social status.



Lastly, it is crucial to address any potential biases or discrimination in the brownfield redevelopment process. This can be achieved through bias training for all stakeholders involved in the redevelopment, including students, managers, and faculty. By promoting awareness and understanding of implicit biases, we can work towards creating a more inclusive and equitable redevelopment process.



In conclusion, social equity is a vital aspect of brownfield redevelopment that must be carefully considered and prioritized by environmental management practitioners. By implementing strategies such as community engagement, affordable housing, access to social services, job creation, and bias training, we can promote a more equitable and inclusive redevelopment process that benefits all members of the community. 





### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:



#### 12.2b Selection of Social Equity Strategies



When it comes to selecting social equity strategies for brownfield redevelopment, environmental management practitioners must consider the unique needs and challenges of each community. This requires a thorough understanding of the community's demographics, history, and current social dynamics.



One approach to selecting social equity strategies is through a participatory process. This involves actively engaging community members in the decision-making process and allowing them to have a say in the selection of strategies. This not only ensures that the strategies align with the community's needs and priorities, but also promotes a sense of ownership and empowerment within the community.



Another important factor to consider is the availability of resources. Some social equity strategies, such as affordable housing and access to social services, may require significant financial investments. Environmental management practitioners must carefully assess the resources available and work with stakeholders to secure additional funding if needed.



Furthermore, the selection of social equity strategies should also take into account the potential trade-offs and unintended consequences. For example, while providing affordable housing may promote social equity, it may also lead to increased traffic and strain on existing infrastructure. Environmental management practitioners must carefully weigh these trade-offs and consider potential mitigation measures.



In addition to these considerations, it is important to continuously monitor and evaluate the effectiveness of the selected social equity strategies. This can help identify any gaps or areas for improvement and inform future decision-making processes.



Overall, the selection of social equity strategies for brownfield redevelopment requires a collaborative and adaptive approach that takes into account the unique needs and challenges of each community. By actively involving community members and carefully considering available resources and potential trade-offs, environmental management practitioners can promote social equity and ensure a more inclusive and sustainable redevelopment process.





### Section: 12.2 Social Equity Strategies:



#### 12.2c Case Studies in Social Equity Strategies



In the previous section, we discussed the importance of selecting social equity strategies for brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will explore some case studies of successful social equity strategies in brownfield redevelopment projects.



One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Lackawanna, New York. This site was once a major steel production facility, but after its closure in the 1980s, it became a brownfield site with significant environmental contamination. The community surrounding the site was predominantly low-income and faced high rates of unemployment.



To address the social equity concerns in this community, the redevelopment project included a number of social equity strategies. This included the creation of affordable housing units, job training programs for local residents, and the establishment of a community center. These strategies not only provided much-needed resources for the community, but also created a sense of ownership and pride among residents.



Another successful example is the redevelopment of the former Ford Motor Company site in Highland Park, Michigan. This site was also a former industrial facility that had been abandoned for decades, leaving behind significant environmental contamination. The community surrounding the site was predominantly low-income and faced high rates of poverty and crime.



To address the social equity concerns in this community, the redevelopment project included a number of social equity strategies. This included the creation of a community garden and urban farm, which provided access to fresh produce for residents and also created job opportunities. The project also included the development of affordable housing units and the establishment of a community health clinic. These strategies not only improved the quality of life for residents, but also helped to revitalize the community.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. By actively engaging with the community and implementing targeted strategies, environmental management practitioners can help to address social inequalities and promote a more equitable society.



In addition to these case studies, there are also a number of resources available for environmental management practitioners to learn more about social equity strategies in brownfield redevelopment. The EPA's Brownfields and Land Revitalization Program provides guidance and resources for incorporating social equity into brownfield redevelopment projects. The National Brownfields Training Conference also offers workshops and sessions on social equity in brownfield redevelopment.



In conclusion, social equity strategies are crucial for promoting a more equitable society and addressing social inequalities in brownfield redevelopment projects. By considering the unique needs and challenges of each community and actively engaging with stakeholders, environmental management practitioners can help to create more inclusive and sustainable communities.





### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. It involves actively involving and empowering community members in the decision-making process and implementation of redevelopment plans. This not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also creates a sense of ownership and pride among residents.



#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity



Community engagement is especially important in marginalized communities, where residents may feel powerless or unimportant within society. In these communities, civic engagement can be a powerful tool for promoting social equity. According to a study, civic engagement can enhance relationships and understanding among diverse individuals, leading to a more cohesive and inclusive community.



One example of the impact of community engagement in promoting social equity can be seen in the case of black youth. Research has shown that black youth who experience racial discrimination are more likely to be aware of and participate in politics. This highlights the importance of addressing social equity concerns in marginalized communities, as it can lead to increased civic engagement and empowerment.



In addition, community engagement can also have a positive impact on at-risk youth, such as African-Americans and Latinos from low-income families living in inner-city neighborhoods. Studies have shown that early participation in civic engagement activities can lead to increased motivation and aspirations for the future among these youth. However, it is important to note that there is no guarantee that this mindset will continue into adulthood, highlighting the need for continued community engagement and support.



Community engagement also plays a crucial role in promoting social equity among immigrant communities. Immigrant parents, in particular, may face challenges in navigating the political system and advocating for their rights. By actively involving these communities in the decision-making process, their voices can be heard and their concerns can be addressed, leading to a more equitable and inclusive society.



In conclusion, community engagement is a vital component of promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. By actively involving and empowering community members, we can create more inclusive and equitable communities, where all individuals have a voice and their needs are addressed. 





### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. It involves actively involving and empowering community members in the decision-making process and implementation of redevelopment plans. This not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also creates a sense of ownership and pride among residents.



#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity

In these communities, civic engagement can be a powerful tool for promoting social equity. Immigrant parents, in particular, may face challenges in navigating the complex systems and policies of their new country. By involving these parents in the decision-making process and providing them with resources and support, community engagement can help bridge the gap between immigrant communities and the larger society, promoting social equity and inclusion.



#### 12.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Social Equity



There are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. These techniques include:



- Community meetings and forums: These provide a platform for community members to voice their concerns and ideas, and to actively participate in the decision-making process.

- Surveys and questionnaires: These can be used to gather feedback and input from community members, ensuring that their needs and concerns are taken into consideration.

- Focus groups: These allow for more in-depth discussions and can provide valuable insights into the needs and perspectives of different community members.

- Community-based organizations: These organizations can serve as intermediaries between the community and the redevelopment project, helping to facilitate communication and collaboration.

- Community outreach and education: This involves actively engaging with the community through events, workshops, and educational programs to increase awareness and understanding of the redevelopment project and its potential impact on the community.



It is important to note that community engagement should not be a one-time event, but an ongoing process throughout the entire brownfield redevelopment project. This ensures that the community remains involved and informed, and that their needs and concerns are continuously addressed. By utilizing these techniques and promoting community engagement, social equity can be effectively integrated into brownfield redevelopment projects, creating a more inclusive and sustainable future for all.





### Section: 12.3 Social Equity and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in promoting social equity in brownfield redevelopment projects. It involves actively involving and empowering community members in the decision-making process and implementation of redevelopment plans. This not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also creates a sense of ownership and pride among residents.



#### 12.3a Role of Community Engagement in Social Equity



Community engagement is especially important in marginalized communities, where residents may feel powerless or unimportant within society. In these communities, civic engagement can be a powerful tool for promoting social equity. According to a study, civic engagement can enhance relationships and understanding among diverse individuals, leading to a more cohesive and inclusive community.



One example of the impact of community engagement in promoting social equity can be seen in the case of black youth. Research has shown that black youth who experience racial discrimination are more likely to be aware of and participate in politics. This highlights the importance of addressing social equity concerns in marginalized communities, as it can lead to increased civic engagement and empowerment.



In addition, community engagement can also have a positive impact on at-risk youth, such as African-Americans and Latinos from low-income families living in inner-city neighborhoods. Studies have shown that early participation in civic engagement activities can lead to increased motivation and aspirations for the future among these youth. However, it is important to note that there is no guarantee that this mindset will continue into adulthood, highlighting the need for continued community engagement and support.
