This helps to lower roof surface temperatures and heat influx, ultimately reducing energy consumption and carbon dioxide emissions from electricity generation.



##### Tree Planting



Tree planting is another commonly used green infrastructure strategy that provides a host of ecological, social, and economic benefits. Trees help to mitigate the urban heat island effect by providing shade and reducing surface temperatures. They also improve air quality by absorbing pollutants and producing oxygen. Trees also provide habitat for wildlife and contribute to the overall aesthetic of an urban environment.



In addition to these benefits, tree planting can also help to reduce stormwater runoff. Trees absorb and store water through their roots, reducing the amount of water that enters the sewer system and waterways. This can help to prevent flooding and reduce the risk of combined sewer overflows. Furthermore, trees can also help to mitigate the effects of climate change by sequestering carbon and reducing the urban heat island effect.



##### Permeable Pavement



Permeable pavement is a type of pavement that allows water to pass through it and into the ground below. This helps to reduce stormwater runoff and replenish groundwater supplies. Permeable pavement can be made from a variety of materials, including concrete, asphalt, and interlocking pavers.



In addition to reducing stormwater runoff, permeable pavement also helps to filter pollutants from the water that passes through it. This can help to improve water quality and protect local ecosystems. Furthermore, permeable pavement can also help to reduce the urban heat island effect by allowing water to evaporate from its surface, cooling the surrounding area.



#### 14.2b Selection of Green Infrastructure Strategies



When selecting green infrastructure strategies for a brownfield redevelopment project, it is important to consider the specific site conditions and goals of the project. Factors such as soil type, topography, and climate can all impact the effectiveness of different strategies. Additionally, the goals of the project, such as reducing stormwater runoff or improving air quality, should also be taken into account.



It is also important to consider the maintenance requirements and costs associated with each green infrastructure strategy. Some strategies may require more frequent maintenance or have higher upfront costs, but may provide greater long-term benefits. It is important to weigh these factors when making decisions about which strategies to implement.



In some cases, a combination of green infrastructure strategies may be the most effective approach. For example, a project may incorporate green roofs, tree planting, and permeable pavement to achieve multiple benefits such as reducing stormwater runoff, improving air quality, and mitigating the urban heat island effect.



Overall, the selection of green infrastructure strategies should be carefully considered and tailored to the specific needs and goals of each brownfield redevelopment project. By incorporating these strategies, we can create more sustainable and resilient urban environments while also providing numerous ecological, economic, and social benefits.





### Section: 14.2 Green Infrastructure Strategies:



Green infrastructure strategies are becoming increasingly popular in brownfield redevelopment projects due to their effectiveness in providing ecological, economic, and social benefits. These strategies utilize natural systems and processes to manage water and create healthier urban environments. In this section, we will provide an overview of some common green infrastructure strategies and their benefits.



#### 14.2a Overview of Green Infrastructure Strategies



Green roofs, tree planting, and permeable pavement are some of the most commonly used green infrastructure strategies. These strategies can be implemented individually or in combination to achieve maximum benefits.



##### Green Roofs



A green roof is a rooftop that is partially or completely covered with vegetation. It includes additional layers such as a root barrier, drainage, and irrigation systems. Green roofs can be categorized as extensive (with a growing media depth ranging from two to six inches) or intensive (with a growing media depth greater than six inches).



Green roofs provide numerous benefits, including reducing stormwater runoff by storing water in the growing media. This reduces the burden on the sewer system and waterways, decreasing the risk of combined sewer overflows. Additionally, green roofs reduce energy usage by providing insulation, reducing solar radiation on the roof's surface, and providing evaporative cooling. This helps to lower roof surface temperatures and heat influx, ultimately reducing energy consumption and carbon dioxide emissions from electricity generation.



##### Tree Planting



Tree planting is another commonly used green infrastructure strategy that provides a host of ecological, social, and economic benefits. Trees help to mitigate the urban heat island effect by providing shade and reducing surface temperatures. They also improve air quality by absorbing pollutants and producing oxygen. Trees also provide habitat for wildlife and contribute to the overall aesthetic of an urban environment.



In addition to these benefits, tree planting also has economic advantages. Trees can increase property values and attract businesses and tourists to an area. They also provide cost savings by reducing energy usage for heating and cooling buildings.



##### Permeable Pavement



Permeable pavement is a type of pavement that allows water to pass through it and into the ground below. This helps to reduce stormwater runoff and replenish groundwater supplies. Permeable pavement can be made from a variety of materials, including concrete, asphalt, and interlocking pavers.



In addition to managing stormwater, permeable pavement also helps to reduce the urban heat island effect by allowing water to evaporate from its surface, cooling the surrounding area. It also reduces the need for traditional stormwater management infrastructure, saving costs for developers and municipalities.



#### 14.2b Benefits of Green Infrastructure Strategies



Green infrastructure strategies provide a range of benefits, including ecological, economic, and social advantages. These strategies help to create more sustainable and resilient communities by managing stormwater, reducing energy consumption, and improving air quality.



##### Ecological Benefits



Green infrastructure strategies help to restore natural processes and systems that are often disrupted by urban development. By managing stormwater, these strategies reduce the burden on traditional stormwater management infrastructure and help to replenish groundwater supplies. They also provide habitat for wildlife and contribute to biodiversity in urban areas.



##### Economic Benefits



Green infrastructure strategies can provide significant cost savings for developers and municipalities. By reducing the need for traditional stormwater management infrastructure, these strategies can save on construction and maintenance costs. They also provide energy savings by reducing the need for heating and cooling buildings, ultimately leading to cost savings for building owners.



##### Social Benefits



Green infrastructure strategies also have social benefits, such as improving air quality and creating more livable and attractive communities. By reducing the urban heat island effect, these strategies help to create cooler and more comfortable urban environments. They also provide opportunities for recreation and green spaces, contributing to the overall well-being of residents.



#### 14.2c Case Studies in Green Infrastructure Strategies



To further illustrate the benefits and effectiveness of green infrastructure strategies, let's take a look at some case studies of successful implementation.



##### Case Study 1: The High Line, New York City



The High Line is a 1.45-mile-long elevated park built on an abandoned railway line in New York City. The park features green roofs, permeable pavement, and rain gardens, among other green infrastructure elements. These strategies help to manage stormwater, reduce the urban heat island effect, and provide habitat for wildlife. The High Line has become a popular tourist attraction and has contributed to the revitalization of the surrounding neighborhood.



##### Case Study 2: The Green Alleys, Chicago



The Green Alleys project in Chicago transformed over 100 miles of alleys into permeable pavement and green infrastructure corridors. These alleys help to manage stormwater and reduce the urban heat island effect, while also providing safer and more attractive spaces for pedestrians and cyclists. The project has received numerous awards and has become a model for other cities looking to implement green infrastructure strategies.



##### Case Study 3: The Bioswale Project, Portland



The Bioswale Project in Portland, Oregon, is a network of over 1,000 bioswales (vegetated ditches) that help to manage stormwater and improve water quality. These bioswales also provide habitat for wildlife and contribute to the overall aesthetic of the city. The project has been successful in reducing stormwater runoff and has received recognition for its innovative approach to green infrastructure.



#### Conclusion



Green infrastructure strategies are an effective and sustainable approach to managing stormwater and creating healthier urban environments. These strategies provide a range of benefits, including ecological, economic, and social advantages. By implementing green infrastructure strategies, we can create more resilient and livable communities while also mitigating the impacts of urban development on the environment. 





### Section: 14.3 Green Infrastructure and Community Engagement:



Green infrastructure strategies are an essential component of brownfield redevelopment projects, providing a sustainable and holistic approach to managing urban environments. However, the success of these strategies relies heavily on community engagement. In this section, we will discuss the role of community engagement in green infrastructure and its importance in achieving successful brownfield redevelopment.



#### 14.3a Role of Community Engagement in Green Infrastructure



Community engagement is a crucial aspect of green infrastructure implementation, as it involves the active participation of community members in the planning, design, and maintenance of green infrastructure projects. This engagement can take various forms, such as public meetings, workshops, surveys, and focus groups. The goal of community engagement is to involve community members in decision-making processes and ensure that their needs and concerns are addressed.



One of the primary benefits of community engagement in green infrastructure is the creation of a sense of ownership and pride among community members. By involving them in the planning and design process, community members feel a sense of responsibility towards the project and are more likely to support and maintain it in the long run. This can lead to a more sustainable and successful implementation of green infrastructure strategies.



Moreover, community engagement can also provide valuable insights and local knowledge that can inform the design and implementation of green infrastructure projects. Community members are often the best source of information about the local environment, including potential challenges and opportunities for green infrastructure. By involving them in the process, designers and planners can ensure that the project is tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of the community.



Community engagement also plays a crucial role in promoting social equity and justice in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in decision-making processes, their voices and concerns are heard and addressed, leading to a more equitable distribution of benefits and resources. This can help to mitigate any potential negative impacts of green infrastructure, such as gentrification or displacement of vulnerable communities.



In addition to these benefits, community engagement also helps to build trust and foster relationships between community members and project stakeholders. This can lead to a more collaborative and cooperative approach to brownfield redevelopment, where all parties work together towards a common goal. This can ultimately result in a more successful and sustainable implementation of green infrastructure strategies.



In conclusion, community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of green infrastructure in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the planning, design, and maintenance of green infrastructure projects, we can create a more sustainable, equitable, and community-driven approach to managing urban environments. 





### Section: 14.3 Green Infrastructure and Community Engagement:



Green infrastructure strategies are an essential component of brownfield redevelopment projects, providing a sustainable and holistic approach to managing urban environments. However, the success of these strategies relies heavily on community engagement. In this section, we will discuss the techniques for engaging the community in green infrastructure and its importance in achieving successful brownfield redevelopment.



#### 14.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Green Infrastructure



Community engagement is a crucial aspect of green infrastructure implementation, as it involves the active participation of community members in the planning, design, and maintenance of green infrastructure projects. There are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in green infrastructure, and each has its own benefits and challenges.



One technique is the use of public meetings, where community members are invited to attend and provide feedback on green infrastructure projects. These meetings can be held at different stages of the project, such as during the planning and design phase, as well as during the implementation and maintenance phase. Public meetings allow for direct communication between community members and project planners, and can help to address any concerns or questions that the community may have.



Another technique is the use of workshops, where community members are actively involved in the planning and design process. Workshops can be used to gather local knowledge and insights from community members, and to incorporate their ideas and suggestions into the project. This not only helps to create a sense of ownership and pride among community members, but also ensures that the project is tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of the community.



Surveys and focus groups are also effective techniques for engaging the community in green infrastructure. Surveys can be distributed to a larger group of community members, allowing for a wider range of perspectives and feedback. Focus groups, on the other hand, involve a smaller group of community members who are selected based on their expertise or interest in the project. Both techniques provide valuable insights and feedback from the community, which can inform the design and implementation of green infrastructure projects.



In addition to these techniques, the use of social media and online platforms can also be effective in engaging the community in green infrastructure. These platforms allow for easy communication and information sharing, and can reach a larger audience. They also provide a space for community members to voice their opinions and concerns, and for project planners to address them in a timely manner.



Overall, the techniques for engaging the community in green infrastructure are crucial for the success of brownfield redevelopment projects. By involving community members in the process, project planners can ensure that the project meets the needs and concerns of the community, leading to a more sustainable and successful implementation of green infrastructure strategies. 





### Section: 14.3 Green Infrastructure and Community Engagement:



Green infrastructure strategies are an essential component of brownfield redevelopment projects, providing a sustainable and holistic approach to managing urban environments. However, the success of these strategies relies heavily on community engagement. In this section, we will discuss the techniques for engaging the community in green infrastructure and its importance in achieving successful brownfield redevelopment.



#### 14.3c Case Studies in Community Engagement and Green Infrastructure



Community engagement is crucial for the successful implementation of green infrastructure in brownfield redevelopment projects. In this subsection, we will explore some case studies that highlight the importance of community engagement and its impact on green infrastructure projects.



One such case study is the redevelopment of the South Bronx in New York City. The South Bronx was once a heavily industrialized area with numerous brownfield sites, leading to environmental degradation and health issues for the community. In the 1990s, community members, along with local organizations and government agencies, came together to revitalize the area through green infrastructure projects. This involved converting vacant lots into community gardens, creating green roofs on buildings, and implementing rain gardens and bioswales to manage stormwater runoff. The success of these projects was largely due to the active involvement of community members in the planning and implementation process. This not only improved the environmental conditions of the South Bronx but also created a sense of ownership and pride among community members.



Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Baltimore, Maryland. This site was once a major steel manufacturing plant, but after its closure, it became a brownfield site with contaminated soil and water. The community, along with local organizations and government agencies, worked together to transform the site into a mixed-use development with green infrastructure features. This included the creation of a green roof on a parking garage, the installation of rain gardens and permeable pavement, and the restoration of a nearby stream. The community was actively involved in the planning and design process, providing valuable insights and ideas that were incorporated into the final project. This not only improved the environmental conditions of the area but also created a sense of community pride and ownership.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of community engagement in green infrastructure projects. By involving community members in the planning, design, and implementation process, projects can be tailored to the specific needs and characteristics of the community, leading to greater success and sustainability. Additionally, community engagement fosters a sense of ownership and pride among community members, creating a more resilient and connected community. 





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the concept of brownfield redevelopment and its potential for incorporating green infrastructure. We have seen how brownfield sites, which are abandoned or underutilized industrial or commercial properties, can be transformed into sustainable and environmentally friendly spaces through the implementation of green infrastructure practices. These practices not only improve the overall health and well-being of the community, but also provide economic benefits and promote social equity.



We have discussed various types of green infrastructure, such as green roofs, rain gardens, and permeable pavement, and how they can be integrated into brownfield redevelopment projects. We have also highlighted the importance of considering the site's history and potential contamination when planning for green infrastructure. By conducting thorough environmental assessments and remediation, we can ensure that the redevelopment process is safe and sustainable.



Furthermore, we have examined the role of stakeholders in brownfield redevelopment and how collaboration between government agencies, private developers, and community members is crucial for the success of these projects. By involving all stakeholders in the planning and decision-making process, we can create a more inclusive and equitable environment for all.



Overall, brownfield redevelopment and green infrastructure go hand in hand in creating sustainable and resilient communities. By repurposing underutilized land and incorporating green practices, we can revitalize our cities and promote a healthier and more sustainable future.

#### Exercise 1: Identifying Brownfield Sites

Research and identify three potential brownfield sites in your local area. What types of industries were previously located on these sites? How could green infrastructure be incorporated into their redevelopment plans?



#### Exercise 2: Calculating Economic Benefits

Using the information provided in this chapter, calculate the potential economic benefits of implementing green infrastructure in a brownfield redevelopment project. Consider factors such as reduced stormwater management costs, increased property values, and job creation.



#### Exercise 3: Community Engagement

Develop a community engagement plan for a brownfield redevelopment project. How will you involve all stakeholders in the decision-making process? What strategies will you use to ensure inclusivity and equity?



#### Exercise 4: Environmental Assessment

Choose a brownfield site and conduct an environmental assessment. What potential contaminants could be present on the site? How would you remediate these contaminants to ensure the safety and sustainability of the redevelopment project?



#### Exercise 5: Green Infrastructure Design

Design a green infrastructure plan for a brownfield site of your choice. Consider the site's history, potential contaminants, and surrounding community. How will your design promote sustainability, social equity, and economic benefits? 





## Chapter: Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



### Introduction:



Brownfield redevelopment is a crucial aspect of environmental management, as it involves the revitalization of previously contaminated or underutilized land. This process not only improves the physical appearance of the land, but also has significant economic, social, and environmental benefits. In this chapter, we will explore the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and renewable energy, and how these two concepts can work together to create sustainable and environmentally-friendly solutions.



The redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to incorporate renewable energy sources into the design and construction of new developments. This can include the installation of solar panels, wind turbines, or geothermal systems, among others. By utilizing renewable energy, these developments can reduce their carbon footprint and contribute to the overall goal of mitigating climate change.



In addition to the environmental benefits, brownfield redevelopment also has economic advantages. By repurposing previously contaminated land, developers can save on the costs of acquiring new land and avoid the potential liabilities associated with developing on pristine land. Furthermore, the use of renewable energy can lead to long-term cost savings for both developers and future occupants of the redeveloped site.



This chapter will delve into the various strategies and considerations involved in incorporating renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment projects. We will also discuss case studies and best practices to provide a comprehensive understanding of this important topic. By the end of this chapter, readers will have a better understanding of how brownfield redevelopment and renewable energy can work together to create sustainable and successful developments.





### Section: 15.1 Renewable Energy and Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment presents a unique opportunity to incorporate renewable energy sources into the design and construction of new developments. Renewable energy is energy from naturally replenished resources such as sunlight, wind, water, and geothermal heat. These sources are considered sustainable as they are naturally replenished on a human timescale. In contrast, non-renewable energy sources, such as fossil fuels and nuclear energy, are finite and will eventually run out.



The use of renewable energy in brownfield redevelopment projects has significant environmental benefits. By utilizing renewable energy sources, these developments can reduce their carbon footprint and contribute to the overall goal of mitigating climate change. This is especially important in the context of brownfield redevelopment, as these sites often have a history of contamination and pollution. By incorporating renewable energy, developers can help to offset the environmental impact of the site's previous use.



In addition to the environmental benefits, there are also economic advantages to incorporating renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment projects. By repurposing previously contaminated land, developers can save on the costs of acquiring new land and avoid potential liabilities associated with developing on pristine land. Furthermore, the use of renewable energy can lead to long-term cost savings for both developers and future occupants of the redeveloped site.



One of the key considerations when incorporating renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment is the choice of energy source. Solar panels, wind turbines, and geothermal systems are all viable options, but the most suitable choice will depend on factors such as location, climate, and available resources. For example, a site with ample sunlight may be better suited for solar panels, while a site with strong winds may be better suited for wind turbines.



Another important consideration is the integration of renewable energy into the overall design of the development. This includes factors such as the placement and orientation of solar panels or wind turbines, as well as the incorporation of energy storage systems. Proper integration can maximize the efficiency and effectiveness of renewable energy sources, leading to greater cost savings and environmental benefits.



To better understand the successful integration of renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment projects, it is helpful to examine case studies and best practices. For example, the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Lackawanna, New York, incorporated a 2.4-megawatt solar array, making it one of the largest solar installations on a brownfield site in the United States. This project not only helped to revitalize the site, but also provided clean energy to the surrounding community.



In conclusion, the incorporation of renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment projects has numerous benefits, including environmental, economic, and social. By carefully considering the choice of energy source and proper integration into the development design, developers can create sustainable and successful projects that contribute to the overall goal of mitigating climate change.

#### 15.1b Role of Renewable Energy in Brownfield Redevelopment



The role of renewable energy in brownfield redevelopment is multifaceted. Not only does it provide environmental and economic benefits, but it also plays a crucial role in promoting sustainable development and mitigating the effects of climate change. By incorporating renewable energy into the design and construction of brownfield redevelopment projects, developers can contribute to the overall goal of creating a more sustainable and environmentally friendly built environment.



One of the key benefits of renewable energy in brownfield redevelopment is its ability to reduce the carbon footprint of the development. By utilizing renewable energy sources, developers can significantly decrease the amount of greenhouse gas emissions produced by the site. This is especially important in the context of brownfield redevelopment, as these sites often have a history of contamination and pollution. By incorporating renewable energy, developers can help to offset the environmental impact of the site's previous use and promote a more sustainable future.



In addition to reducing the carbon footprint, renewable energy also has the potential to provide long-term cost savings for both developers and future occupants of the redeveloped site. By utilizing renewable energy sources, developers can decrease their reliance on non-renewable energy sources, which are often subject to price fluctuations. This can lead to significant cost savings over time, making the development more economically viable in the long run.



Furthermore, the use of renewable energy in brownfield redevelopment can also have a positive impact on the surrounding community. By repurposing previously contaminated land, developers can help to revitalize the area and create new opportunities for economic growth. This can lead to job creation and increased property values, benefiting both the community and the developers.



The choice of renewable energy source is also an important consideration in brownfield redevelopment. Solar panels, wind turbines, and geothermal systems all have their own unique advantages and disadvantages, and the most suitable choice will depend on the specific characteristics of the site. For example, a site with ample sunlight may be better suited for solar panels, while a site with strong winds may be better suited for wind turbines.



In conclusion, the role of renewable energy in brownfield redevelopment is crucial in promoting sustainable development and mitigating the effects of climate change. By incorporating renewable energy sources into the design and construction of brownfield redevelopment projects, developers can create a more environmentally friendly and economically viable built environment. This not only benefits the developers and future occupants of the site, but also the surrounding community and the planet as a whole.





### Section: 15.1 Renewable Energy and Brownfields:

#### 15.1c Case Studies in Renewable Energy and Brownfield Redevelopment



To further illustrate the benefits and potential of incorporating renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment, this subsection will explore some case studies of successful projects.



One notable example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel plant in Lackawanna, New York. The site, which was once a major source of pollution and contamination, has been transformed into a renewable energy hub. The site now hosts a solar farm, wind turbines, and a hydroelectric plant, providing clean energy to the surrounding community.



Another successful project is the redevelopment of the former Ford Motor Company assembly plant in Richmond, California. The site, which was heavily contaminated with industrial waste, has been transformed into a mixed-use development that includes a solar farm and a geothermal heating and cooling system. This project not only provides clean energy, but also creates jobs and revitalizes the local economy.



These case studies demonstrate the potential for brownfield redevelopment to not only clean up contaminated sites, but also contribute to the growth of renewable energy. By repurposing these sites, developers can help to mitigate the effects of climate change and create sustainable communities.





### Section: 15.2 Renewable Energy Strategies:



Renewable energy strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. These strategies not only have significant environmental benefits, but also offer economic advantages for developers and future occupants of the site. In this section, we will provide an overview of the different renewable energy strategies that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 15.2a Overview of Renewable Energy Strategies



There are several renewable energy sources that can be utilized in brownfield redevelopment projects, including solar, wind, and geothermal energy. Each of these sources has its own unique advantages and considerations, and the most suitable choice will depend on the specific characteristics of the site.



Solar energy is one of the most commonly used renewable energy sources in brownfield redevelopment. Solar panels can be installed on rooftops or on the ground, making them a versatile option for a variety of sites. They also have a relatively low maintenance cost and can provide a consistent source of energy throughout the day. However, the effectiveness of solar panels is highly dependent on the amount of sunlight the site receives, making it less suitable for sites in areas with low levels of sunlight.



Wind energy is another popular renewable energy source that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects. Wind turbines can be installed on the site to generate electricity from the wind. This option is more suitable for sites with strong and consistent winds, as the effectiveness of wind turbines is highly dependent on wind speed. However, wind turbines can also be noisy and may not be suitable for sites in close proximity to residential areas.



Geothermal energy is a renewable energy source that utilizes the heat from the Earth's core to generate electricity. This option is more suitable for sites with access to geothermal resources, such as hot springs or geysers. Geothermal systems can also be used for heating and cooling buildings, making them a versatile option for brownfield redevelopment projects. However, the initial installation cost for geothermal systems can be high, and the effectiveness of the system is highly dependent on the availability of geothermal resources.



In addition to these renewable energy sources, there are also other strategies that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects to increase energy efficiency and reduce the overall environmental impact. These strategies include energy-efficient building design, use of energy-efficient appliances and lighting, and implementation of smart energy management systems.



Overall, the choice of renewable energy strategy will depend on the specific characteristics of the site and the goals of the redevelopment project. By carefully considering the available resources and the needs of the site, developers can choose the most suitable renewable energy strategy to maximize the environmental and economic benefits of brownfield redevelopment.





### Section: 15.2 Renewable Energy Strategies:



Renewable energy strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. These strategies not only have significant environmental benefits, but also offer economic advantages for developers and future occupants of the site. In this section, we will provide an overview of the different renewable energy strategies that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 15.2a Overview of Renewable Energy Strategies



There are several renewable energy sources that can be utilized in brownfield redevelopment projects, including solar, wind, and geothermal energy. Each of these sources has its own unique advantages and considerations, and the most suitable choice will depend on the specific characteristics of the site.



Solar energy is one of the most commonly used renewable energy sources in brownfield redevelopment. Solar panels can be installed on rooftops or on the ground, making them a versatile option for a variety of sites. They also have a relatively low maintenance cost and can provide a consistent source of energy throughout the day. However, the effectiveness of solar panels is highly dependent on the amount of sunlight the site receives, making it less suitable for sites in areas with low levels of sunlight.



Wind energy is another popular renewable energy source that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects. Wind turbines can be installed on the site to generate electricity from the wind. This option is more suitable for sites with strong and consistent winds, as the effectiveness of wind turbines is highly dependent on wind speed. However, wind turbines can also be noisy and may not be suitable for sites in close proximity to residential areas.



Geothermal energy is a renewable energy source that utilizes the heat from the Earth's core to generate electricity. This option is more suitable for sites with access to geothermal resources, such as hot springs or geysers. Geothermal energy has the advantage of being a consistent and reliable source of energy, as it is not affected by weather conditions. However, it may not be a feasible option for all brownfield sites, as it requires specific geological conditions.



#### 15.2b Selection of Renewable Energy Strategies



When selecting the most suitable renewable energy strategy for a brownfield redevelopment project, it is important to consider the specific characteristics of the site, as well as the goals and priorities of the project. Factors such as location, available resources, and budget should all be taken into account.



One approach to selecting a renewable energy strategy is to conduct a feasibility study. This involves analyzing the site's energy needs, resources, and potential for renewable energy generation. The results of this study can then be used to determine the most suitable renewable energy strategy for the site.



Another important consideration is the integration of renewable energy into the overall design and development of the brownfield site. This requires collaboration between environmental and energy experts, as well as developers and designers. By incorporating renewable energy strategies into the design from the beginning, the project can maximize its environmental and economic benefits.



In addition to the selection of a specific renewable energy strategy, it is also important to consider the potential for a combination of strategies. For example, a site may have access to both solar and wind resources, and a combination of both strategies may provide a more reliable and cost-effective source of energy.



In conclusion, the selection of renewable energy strategies for brownfield redevelopment projects requires careful consideration of the site's characteristics, goals, and available resources. By incorporating renewable energy into the design and development process, these projects can not only achieve environmental sustainability, but also economic benefits for all stakeholders involved. 





### Section: 15.2 Renewable Energy Strategies:



Renewable energy strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. These strategies not only have significant environmental benefits, but also offer economic advantages for developers and future occupants of the site. In this section, we will provide an overview of the different renewable energy strategies that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 15.2a Overview of Renewable Energy Strategies



There are several renewable energy sources that can be utilized in brownfield redevelopment projects, including solar, wind, and geothermal energy. Each of these sources has its own unique advantages and considerations, and the most suitable choice will depend on the specific characteristics of the site.



Solar energy is one of the most commonly used renewable energy sources in brownfield redevelopment. Solar panels can be installed on rooftops or on the ground, making them a versatile option for a variety of sites. They also have a relatively low maintenance cost and can provide a consistent source of energy throughout the day. However, the effectiveness of solar panels is highly dependent on the amount of sunlight the site receives, making it less suitable for sites in areas with low levels of sunlight.



Wind energy is another popular renewable energy source that can be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects. Wind turbines can be installed on the site to generate electricity from the wind. This option is more suitable for sites with strong and consistent winds, as the effectiveness of wind turbines is highly dependent on wind speed. However, wind turbines can also be noisy and may not be suitable for sites in close proximity to residential areas.



Geothermal energy is a renewable energy source that utilizes the heat from the Earth's core to generate electricity. This option is more suitable for sites with access to geothermal resources, such as hot springs or geysers. Geothermal energy has the advantage of being a constant and reliable source of energy, regardless of weather conditions. However, it may not be feasible for all brownfield sites due to the need for specialized equipment and expertise.



#### 15.2b Case Studies in Renewable Energy Strategies



To further illustrate the potential of renewable energy strategies in brownfield redevelopment, let's examine some case studies of successful projects.



One notable example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Lackawanna, New York. This 1,200-acre site was once a major steel production facility, but had been abandoned for over a decade. The site was contaminated with heavy metals and other pollutants, making it a prime candidate for brownfield redevelopment. The project, known as "Steel Winds," involved the installation of 14 wind turbines on the site, providing enough clean energy to power over 9,000 homes. The project not only cleaned up the site and provided renewable energy, but also created jobs and boosted the local economy.



Another successful case study is the redevelopment of the former Naval Air Station Alameda in California. This 1,500-acre site was once a naval base, but had been abandoned for over 20 years. The site was heavily contaminated with petroleum and other hazardous materials. The redevelopment project, known as "Alameda Point," incorporated a variety of renewable energy strategies, including solar panels, wind turbines, and geothermal heating and cooling systems. These strategies not only provided clean energy for the site, but also reduced the overall energy costs for the occupants.



These case studies demonstrate the potential for renewable energy strategies to not only clean up contaminated sites, but also provide economic benefits and contribute to a more sustainable future. As technology continues to advance and costs decrease, we can expect to see even more successful examples of brownfield redevelopment incorporating renewable energy strategies.





### Section: 15.3 Renewable Energy and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the successful implementation of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss the importance of community engagement in renewable energy projects and the role it plays in promoting energy democracy.



#### 15.3a Role of Community Engagement in Renewable Energy



Community engagement is essential in renewable energy projects as it allows for the participation of the end-user communities in the planning and implementation processes. This not only promotes energy democracy, but also ensures that the project is tailored to the specific needs and concerns of the community. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, community engagement is particularly important as it allows for the integration of renewable energy strategies that align with the community's vision for the site.



However, despite the potential benefits of community engagement, there are challenges that must be addressed. A survey conducted within a community about community renewable energy projects showed that while there was widespread support for implementation, there were low levels of desire for personal involvement. This highlights the need for effective communication and outreach strategies to encourage community participation.



Institutional support is also crucial for the success of community-based renewable energy projects. In the EU and UK, there is a prevalence of institutional support for such projects, leading to a higher number of successful projects compared to the United States. This lack of institutional support in the US is a major barrier to the widespread adoption of community-based renewable energy projects.



However, there has been an increase in market-based investments in community-based solar and wind projects in the US. This is a promising development, as it shows the private sector's growing interest in renewable energy projects that prioritize community engagement. Additionally, the involvement of the private sector can also bring in much-needed resources and expertise to support the implementation of these projects.



In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial aspect of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. It promotes energy democracy and ensures that the project is tailored to the needs and concerns of the community. However, there are challenges that must be addressed, such as low levels of community involvement and lack of institutional support. The involvement of the private sector can also play a significant role in promoting community-based renewable energy projects. 





### Section: 15.3 Renewable Energy and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the successful implementation of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss the importance of community engagement in renewable energy projects and the role it plays in promoting energy democracy.



#### 15.3a Role of Community Engagement in Renewable Energy



Community engagement is essential in renewable energy projects as it allows for the participation of the end-user communities in the planning and implementation processes. This not only promotes energy democracy, but also ensures that the project is tailored to the specific needs and concerns of the community. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, community engagement is particularly important as it allows for the integration of renewable energy strategies that align with the community's vision for the site.



However, despite the potential benefits of community engagement, there are challenges that must be addressed. A survey conducted within a community about community renewable energy projects showed that while there was widespread support for implementation, there were low levels of desire for personal involvement. This highlights the need for effective communication and outreach strategies to encourage community participation.



Institutional support is also crucial for the success of community-based renewable energy projects. In the EU and UK, there is a prevalence of institutional support for such projects, leading to a higher number of successful projects compared to the United States. This lack of institutional support in the US is a major barrier to the widespread adoption of community-based renewable energy projects.



However, there has been an increase in market-based investments in community-based solar and wind projects in the US. This is a promising development, as it shows the private sector's growing interest in renewable energy and community engagement. One example of this is the Solar augmented geothermal energy project, RenewGeo by UC-Won, which incorporates community engagement and energy democracy principles in its planning and implementation processes.



#### 15.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Renewable Energy



To effectively engage the community in renewable energy projects, various techniques can be utilized. One approach is through education and awareness campaigns, such as the Think Resilience online course offered by the Post Carbon Institute. This course not only provides information on renewable energy technologies and issues, but also encourages sustainable and pro-environmental behavior.



Another technique is through community ownership and involvement in the decision-making process. This can be achieved through community meetings, surveys, and workshops where community members can voice their opinions and concerns. This not only promotes energy democracy, but also ensures that the project is tailored to the specific needs and values of the community.



Additionally, partnerships and collaborations with local organizations and institutions can also aid in community engagement. These partnerships can provide resources and expertise, as well as help build trust and credibility within the community.



It is important to note that community engagement should not be a one-time event, but an ongoing process throughout the project's lifespan. Regular communication and updates with the community can help maintain their involvement and support.



In conclusion, community engagement is crucial for the successful implementation of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. By utilizing various techniques and strategies, we can promote energy democracy and ensure that renewable energy projects align with the needs and values of the community. 





### Section: 15.3 Renewable Energy and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the successful implementation of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss the importance of community engagement in renewable energy projects and the role it plays in promoting energy democracy.



#### 15.3a Role of Community Engagement in Renewable Energy



Community engagement is essential in renewable energy projects as it allows for the participation of the end-user communities in the planning and implementation processes. This not only promotes energy democracy, but also ensures that the project is tailored to the specific needs and concerns of the community. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, community engagement is particularly important as it allows for the integration of renewable energy strategies that align with the community's vision for the site.



However, despite the potential benefits of community engagement, there are challenges that must be addressed. A survey conducted within a community about community renewable energy projects showed that while there was widespread support for implementation, there were low levels of desire for personal involvement. This highlights the need for effective communication and outreach strategies to encourage community participation.



Institutional support is also crucial for the success of community-based renewable energy projects. In the EU and UK, there is a prevalence of institutional support for such projects, leading to a higher number of successful projects compared to the United States. This lack of institutional support in the US is a major barrier to the widespread adoption of community-based renewable energy projects.



However, there has been an increase in market-based investments in community-based solar and wind projects in the US. This is a promising development, as it shows the private sector's growing interest in renewable energy and their recognition of the potential benefits of community engagement. For example, community solar projects have gained popularity in recent years, allowing individuals and businesses to invest in and receive credits for renewable energy generation. This not only promotes community involvement, but also helps to reduce the cost of renewable energy for all consumers.



#### 15.3b Case Studies in Community Engagement and Renewable Energy



To further illustrate the importance of community engagement in renewable energy projects, let's take a look at some case studies from around the world.



In Germany, the village of Wildpoldsried has become a model for community-based renewable energy projects. The village has achieved energy self-sufficiency through a combination of solar, wind, and biogas projects, with the majority of the projects owned by the community. This has not only reduced the village's carbon footprint, but has also brought economic benefits to the community through job creation and revenue from energy sales.



In the United Kingdom, the community of Fintry came together to develop a community-owned wind turbine project. The project not only generates renewable energy, but also provides a steady stream of income for the community through the sale of electricity. The community has also used the profits to fund other sustainable projects, such as a community garden and a biomass heating system.



These case studies demonstrate the potential for community-based renewable energy projects to bring about positive social, economic, and environmental impacts. However, it is important to note that these projects were only successful with strong community engagement and institutional support.



#### 15.3c Challenges and Solutions for Community Engagement in Renewable Energy



While community engagement is crucial for the success of renewable energy projects, there are challenges that must be addressed. One major challenge is the lack of knowledge and understanding about renewable energy among community members. This can lead to skepticism and resistance towards renewable energy projects.



To overcome this challenge, effective communication and education strategies must be implemented. This can include community workshops, informational materials, and partnerships with local organizations and leaders. By providing accurate and accessible information, community members can make informed decisions and become more supportive of renewable energy projects.



Another challenge is the unequal distribution of benefits and burdens among community members. In some cases, renewable energy projects may bring about negative impacts, such as noise or visual pollution, to certain individuals or groups. It is important for developers to engage with the community and address these concerns in a transparent and equitable manner.



In conclusion, community engagement is essential for the successful implementation of renewable energy projects, especially in the context of brownfield redevelopment. By promoting energy democracy and tailoring projects to the specific needs and concerns of the community, community engagement can bring about a wide range of positive social, economic, and environmental impacts. However, challenges must be addressed and solutions must be implemented to ensure that community engagement is effective and equitable. 





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we have explored the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and renewable energy. We have seen how the redevelopment of contaminated sites can not only improve the environment, but also provide opportunities for the implementation of renewable energy technologies. By repurposing these sites, we can reduce the need for new development on undeveloped land, preserving natural habitats and promoting sustainable growth.



We have also discussed the various challenges and considerations that come with incorporating renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment projects. These include financial barriers, technical limitations, and community engagement. It is important for environmental managers to carefully assess these factors and develop comprehensive plans to ensure the success of these projects.



Overall, the integration of renewable energy into brownfield redevelopment is a promising approach to addressing both environmental and energy concerns. By utilizing these sites for renewable energy production, we can not only mitigate the effects of climate change, but also revitalize communities and promote economic growth.

## Chapter: Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



### Introduction:



Brownfield redevelopment and adaptive reuse are crucial components of environmental management. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that may have been contaminated by hazardous substances. These properties often pose a threat to public health and the environment, and their redevelopment is essential for revitalizing communities and promoting sustainable land use. In this chapter, we will explore the process of brownfield redevelopment and the various strategies and techniques used to transform these properties into productive and safe spaces. We will also discuss the concept of adaptive reuse, which involves repurposing existing structures for new uses, and its role in brownfield redevelopment. Through this chapter, we hope to provide readers with a comprehensive understanding of the challenges and opportunities associated with brownfield redevelopment and adaptive reuse.





### Section: 16.1 Adaptive Reuse and Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment and adaptive reuse are two important strategies for addressing the issue of abandoned or underutilized properties that may have been contaminated by hazardous substances. These properties, known as brownfields, pose a threat to public health and the environment, and their redevelopment is essential for revitalizing communities and promoting sustainable land use.



#### 16.1a Definition of Adaptive Reuse



Adaptive reuse is the process of repurposing existing structures for new uses. This concept is closely related to the idea of recycling, but instead of materials, it involves reusing buildings and other structures. Adaptive reuse is a sustainable practice that helps reduce waste and conserve resources, as well as preserve historical and cultural landmarks.



Adaptive reuse is particularly relevant in the context of brownfield redevelopment. Many brownfield sites contain old industrial buildings or other structures that are no longer in use. These structures often have historical or architectural value, and adaptive reuse allows them to be repurposed instead of being demolished. This not only preserves the character of the community but also reduces the environmental impact of redevelopment by avoiding the need for new construction.



One example of adaptive reuse in brownfield redevelopment is the conversion of an old factory into a mixed-use development with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. This not only brings new life to the abandoned property but also provides much-needed housing and economic opportunities for the community.



Adaptive reuse also has economic benefits. It is often more cost-effective than new construction, as the existing structure can be renovated and repurposed instead of starting from scratch. This can be especially beneficial for smaller communities or organizations with limited resources.



However, adaptive reuse also has its challenges. The existing structure may not be suitable for the intended use, requiring significant renovations and upgrades. This can be costly and time-consuming, and may also pose safety concerns. Additionally, there may be zoning or regulatory hurdles to overcome, as the existing structure may not comply with current building codes.



Despite these challenges, adaptive reuse is a valuable tool in brownfield redevelopment. It not only promotes sustainable land use and conservation of resources but also contributes to the revitalization of communities and preservation of their history and character. 





### Section: 16.1 Adaptive Reuse and Brownfields:



Adaptive reuse and brownfield redevelopment are two important strategies for addressing the issue of abandoned or underutilized properties that may have been contaminated by hazardous substances. These properties, known as brownfields, pose a threat to public health and the environment, and their redevelopment is essential for revitalizing communities and promoting sustainable land use.
