This not only reduces the cost and environmental impact of traditional remediation methods, but also creates a more sustainable and environmentally-friendly approach to brownfield redevelopment.



#### 18.1c Case Studies in Food Systems and Brownfield Redevelopment



To further illustrate the role of food systems in brownfield redevelopment, let's take a look at some case studies where food systems have been successfully integrated into the remediation and redevelopment process.



One example is the GTRI Agricultural Technology Research Program's work in robotics and automation systems. By incorporating advanced sensors and robotics into food processing industries, they have been able to improve productivity and efficiency while also reducing the risk of worker injury. This not only benefits the food industry, but also contributes to the overall sustainability of the brownfield redevelopment process.



Another example is the use of advanced imaging and sensor concepts in grading and inspection of food products. By utilizing technologies such as stereo 3D, time-of-flight, and UV imaging, researchers have been able to improve the quality and safety of food products, making them more marketable and reducing waste. This not only benefits the food industry, but also contributes to the economic viability of brownfield redevelopment.



In addition, the GTRI Agricultural Technology Research Program's focus on environmental and energy systems has also played a role in brownfield redevelopment. By developing technologies to reduce water usage and waste generation, as well as recovering waste heat and byproducts from processing operations, they have helped to make the food industry more sustainable and environmentally-friendly. This not only benefits the industry, but also contributes to the overall sustainability of brownfield redevelopment.



Overall, these case studies demonstrate the important role that food systems play in brownfield redevelopment. By integrating food systems into the remediation and redevelopment process, we can create more sustainable and resilient communities while also promoting economic growth and improving access to fresh, healthy food. 





### Section: 18.2 Food Systems Strategies:



Food systems play a crucial role in the remediation and redevelopment of brownfields. In this section, we will explore the various strategies that can be employed to integrate food systems into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 18.2a Overview of Food Systems Strategies



There are several strategies that can be used to incorporate food systems into brownfield redevelopment. These strategies can be broadly categorized into two main approaches: utilizing food systems to support the remediation process and utilizing food systems to support the redevelopment process.



One strategy for utilizing food systems in the remediation process is through phytoremediation. As mentioned in the previous section, certain plants have the ability to absorb and break down contaminants in the soil. This process can be used to naturally clean up brownfield sites, reducing the cost and environmental impact of traditional remediation methods. Additionally, this approach can also create opportunities for urban agriculture and food production on the remediated land.



Another strategy for incorporating food systems into brownfield remediation is through the use of composting. Composting is the process of decomposing organic waste into nutrient-rich soil. This soil can then be used to remediate contaminated land, as well as support urban agriculture and food production. Composting not only reduces the amount of waste sent to landfills, but also provides a sustainable and cost-effective method for remediating brownfields.



In terms of utilizing food systems in the redevelopment process, one strategy is to incorporate urban agriculture and food production into the design of the redevelopment project. This can include community gardens, rooftop gardens, and urban farms. By repurposing abandoned or underutilized land, brownfield redevelopment can create space for these food production sites, increasing access to fresh, healthy food in underserved communities.



Another strategy is to incorporate food systems into the design of the built environment. This can include features such as green roofs, rain gardens, and permeable pavement, which can help to mitigate stormwater runoff and reduce the risk of flooding. These features not only support sustainable food production, but also contribute to the overall resilience of the built environment.



In addition to these strategies, it is important to consider the social and economic aspects of food systems in brownfield redevelopment. This includes promoting equitable access to fresh, healthy food in underserved communities, as well as supporting local food businesses and creating job opportunities in the food sector.



Overall, integrating food systems into brownfield redevelopment projects can have numerous benefits, including promoting sustainable and resilient food systems, supporting the remediation process, and contributing to economic growth and community development. By utilizing these strategies, we can create more holistic and sustainable solutions for brownfield redevelopment.





### Section: 18.2 Food Systems Strategies:



Food systems play a crucial role in the remediation and redevelopment of brownfields. In this section, we will explore the various strategies that can be employed to integrate food systems into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 18.2a Overview of Food Systems Strategies



There are several strategies that can be used to incorporate food systems into brownfield redevelopment. These strategies can be broadly categorized into two main approaches: utilizing food systems to support the remediation process and utilizing food systems to support the redevelopment process.



One strategy for utilizing food systems in the remediation process is through phytoremediation. As mentioned in the previous section, certain plants have the ability to absorb and break down contaminants in the soil. This process can be used to naturally clean up brownfield sites, reducing the cost and environmental impact of traditional remediation methods. Additionally, this approach can also create opportunities for urban agriculture and food production on the remediated land.



Another strategy for incorporating food systems into brownfield remediation is through the use of composting. Composting is the process of decomposing organic waste into nutrient-rich soil. This soil can then be used to remediate contaminated land, as well as support urban agriculture and food production. Composting not only reduces the amount of waste sent to landfills, but also provides a sustainable and cost-effective method for remediating brownfields.



In terms of utilizing food systems in the redevelopment process, one strategy is to incorporate urban agriculture and food production into the design of the redevelopment project. This can include community gardens, rooftop gardens, and urban farms. By repurposing abandoned or underutilized land, brownfield redevelopment can create space for these food production sites, increasing access to fresh, healthy food in underserved communities.



#### 18.2b Selection of Food Systems Strategies



When selecting food systems strategies for brownfield redevelopment, it is important to consider the specific needs and challenges of the site. Factors such as the type and extent of contamination, the surrounding community, and the goals of the redevelopment project should all be taken into account.



One key consideration is the type of contaminants present on the site. Different plants and composting methods are more effective at remediating certain types of contaminants. For example, plants with deep root systems are better at absorbing heavy metals, while plants with fibrous roots are better at breaking down organic contaminants. Similarly, certain composting methods may be more effective at breaking down specific types of contaminants.



The surrounding community should also be considered when selecting food systems strategies. Community engagement and input can help ensure that the chosen strategies align with the needs and desires of the community. Additionally, the availability of resources and expertise within the community can also influence the selection of strategies.



Finally, the goals of the redevelopment project should be taken into account. If the primary goal is to remediate the site, then strategies that prioritize phytoremediation and composting may be the best option. However, if the goal is to create a sustainable and resilient community, then incorporating urban agriculture and food production into the design of the project may be more beneficial.



In conclusion, the selection of food systems strategies for brownfield redevelopment should be a thoughtful and collaborative process, taking into account the specific needs and goals of the site and community. By incorporating food systems into brownfield redevelopment, we can not only remediate contaminated land, but also create sustainable and resilient communities.





### Section: 18.2 Food Systems Strategies:



Food systems play a crucial role in the remediation and redevelopment of brownfields. In this section, we will explore the various strategies that can be employed to integrate food systems into brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 18.2a Overview of Food Systems Strategies



There are several strategies that can be used to incorporate food systems into brownfield redevelopment. These strategies can be broadly categorized into two main approaches: utilizing food systems to support the remediation process and utilizing food systems to support the redevelopment process.



One strategy for utilizing food systems in the remediation process is through phytoremediation. As mentioned in the previous section, certain plants have the ability to absorb and break down contaminants in the soil. This process can be used to naturally clean up brownfield sites, reducing the cost and environmental impact of traditional remediation methods. Additionally, this approach can also create opportunities for urban agriculture and food production on the remediated land.



Another strategy for incorporating food systems into brownfield remediation is through the use of composting. Composting is the process of decomposing organic waste into nutrient-rich soil. This soil can then be used to remediate contaminated land, as well as support urban agriculture and food production. Composting not only reduces the amount of waste sent to landfills, but also provides a sustainable and cost-effective method for remediating brownfields.



In terms of utilizing food systems in the redevelopment process, one strategy is to incorporate urban agriculture and food production into the design of the redevelopment project. This can include community gardens, rooftop gardens, and urban farms. By repurposing abandoned or underutilized land, brownfield redevelopment can create space for these food production sites, increasing access to fresh, healthy food in underserved communities.



#### 18.2b Food Systems and Resilience



In addition to supporting the remediation and redevelopment processes, food systems can also contribute to the resilience of brownfield communities. Resilience-building involves a mix of prevention, anticipation, and the capacity to absorb, adapt, and transform following a disruption. By incorporating food systems into brownfield redevelopment, we can address multiple elements of resilience.



One element is diverse food sourcing. Diverse sourcing of food, such as through international trade, can help buffer the food supply against shocks and stresses. This is especially important for brownfield communities, which may already face challenges in accessing fresh, healthy food. By diversifying the sources of food, we can reduce the impact of disruptions on the food supply.



Another element is diverse food supply chain types. A mix of traditional, transitional, and modern food supply chains can help buffer shocks and stresses of different types. For example, traditional food supply chains may be more resilient to natural disasters, while modern food supply chains may be more resilient to economic shocks. By incorporating a mix of supply chain types, we can increase the overall resilience of the food system.



#### 18.2c Case Studies in Food Systems Strategies



To further illustrate the potential of food systems in brownfield redevelopment, let's explore some case studies of successful projects.



One example is the Fresh Moves Mobile Market in Chicago, Illinois. This project repurposed an old city bus into a mobile market that brings fresh produce to underserved communities. The bus travels to different locations throughout the city, providing access to fresh, healthy food for residents who may not have easy access to grocery stores.



Another example is the Growing Power project in Milwaukee, Wisconsin. This project transformed an abandoned brownfield site into a thriving urban farm. The farm not only produces fresh produce for the community, but also serves as a training center for urban agriculture and sustainable food systems.



These case studies demonstrate the potential for food systems to not only support the remediation and redevelopment of brownfields, but also to contribute to the resilience and well-being of the surrounding communities. By incorporating food systems into brownfield redevelopment, we can create more sustainable and resilient communities for the future.





### Section: 18.3 Food Systems and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of food systems in brownfield redevelopment projects. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which community engagement can be utilized to support and enhance food systems in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 18.3a Role of Community Engagement in Food Systems



Community engagement is essential in promoting and sustaining local food systems. By involving community members in the planning and implementation of food systems in brownfield redevelopment, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of the community are taken into account. This not only increases the likelihood of success for these projects, but also fosters a sense of ownership and pride within the community.



One way in which community engagement can be utilized is through participatory action research (PAR). PAR is an approach to research that involves collaboration between researchers and community members to address a specific issue or problem. In the context of food systems and brownfield redevelopment, PAR can be used to gather input and feedback from community members on the design and implementation of food production sites. This not only ensures that the needs and preferences of the community are considered, but also empowers community members to take an active role in the redevelopment process.



Another way in which community engagement can support food systems in brownfield redevelopment is through education and outreach. By educating community members about the benefits of local food systems and involving them in the process, we can increase awareness and support for these initiatives. This can also lead to increased participation in community gardens and other food production sites, creating a sense of community and promoting healthy eating habits.



In addition to education and outreach, community engagement can also play a role in addressing issues of food insecurity and access to healthy food. In low-income communities, which are often located near brownfield sites, access to fresh, healthy food can be limited. By involving community members in the design and implementation of food systems in these areas, we can ensure that these initiatives are tailored to the specific needs and challenges of the community. This can include strategies such as community-supported agriculture (CSA) programs, which provide affordable access to fresh produce for community members.



Overall, community engagement is a crucial component of successful food systems in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the planning and implementation process, we can create sustainable and inclusive food systems that benefit both the environment and the community. 





### Section: 18.3 Food Systems and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of food systems in brownfield redevelopment projects. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which community engagement can be utilized to support and enhance food systems in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 18.3a Role of Community Engagement in Food Systems



Community engagement is essential in promoting and sustaining local food systems. By involving community members in the planning and implementation of food systems in brownfield redevelopment, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of the community are taken into account. This not only increases the likelihood of success for these projects, but also fosters a sense of ownership and pride within the community.



One way in which community engagement can be utilized is through participatory action research (PAR). PAR is an approach to research that involves collaboration between researchers and community members to address a specific issue or problem. In the context of food systems and brownfield redevelopment, PAR can be used to gather input and feedback from community members on the design and implementation of food production sites. This not only ensures that the needs and preferences of the community are considered, but also empowers community members to take an active role in the redevelopment process.



Another way in which community engagement can support food systems in brownfield redevelopment is through education and outreach. By educating community members about the benefits of local food systems and involving them in the process, we can increase awareness and support for these initiatives. This can also lead to increased participation in community gardens and other food production sites, creating a sense of community and promoting healthy eating habits.



In addition to education and outreach, community engagement can also play a role in addressing issues of food insecurity within the community. By involving community members in the planning and implementation of food systems, we can ensure that the needs of food insecure individuals are taken into account. This can include providing access to affordable and nutritious food options, as well as creating job training programs and other economic opportunities within the food system.



#### 18.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Food Systems



There are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in food systems in brownfield redevelopment. These techniques can range from short-term approaches to more long-lasting solutions.



One short-term approach is to ensure that community members are aware of existing food assistance programs, social services, and job training workshops in their community. This can help to address immediate food insecurity and provide resources for individuals to improve their economic situation.



Another short-term approach is to connect social services with the food system. This can involve partnerships between dietitians and farmers to create programs such as community supported agriculture (CSA) and place-based institutional procurement strategies. These initiatives not only promote healthy eating habits, but also support local farmers and strengthen the community's food system.



For more long-lasting solutions, changes in the food system of a community may be necessary. This can involve a shift from temporary solutions, such as food banks, to more sustainable options like community gardens. Community gardens not only provide access to fresh and nutritious food, but also teach valuable skills in food production and increase self-reliance within the community.



Community development is also crucial for success in food systems and brownfield redevelopment. By connecting individuals who may ordinarily remain isolated from each other, we can foster a sense of community and commitment to long-term solutions. This can involve community members taking an active role in the planning and implementation of food systems, as well as advocating for policies that support local food production.



In conclusion, community engagement is a vital component of successful food systems in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the planning and implementation process, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of the community are taken into account. This not only promotes a sense of ownership and pride within the community, but also leads to more sustainable and equitable food systems. 





### Section: 18.3 Food Systems and Community Engagement:



Community engagement plays a crucial role in the success of food systems in brownfield redevelopment projects. In this section, we will explore the various ways in which community engagement can be utilized to support and enhance food systems in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 18.3a Role of Community Engagement in Food Systems



Community engagement is essential in promoting and sustaining local food systems. By involving community members in the planning and implementation of food systems in brownfield redevelopment, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of the community are taken into account. This not only increases the likelihood of success for these projects, but also fosters a sense of ownership and pride within the community.



One way in which community engagement can be utilized is through participatory action research (PAR). PAR is an approach to research that involves collaboration between researchers and community members to address a specific issue or problem. In the context of food systems and brownfield redevelopment, PAR can be used to gather input and feedback from community members on the design and implementation of food production sites. This not only ensures that the needs and preferences of the community are considered, but also empowers community members to take an active role in the redevelopment process.



PAR can also be a valuable tool in addressing issues of food insecurity within the community. By involving community members in the research process, PAR can help to identify the root causes of food insecurity and develop effective solutions that are tailored to the specific needs of the community. This not only helps to improve food access and availability, but also promotes community empowerment and social change.



Another way in which community engagement can support food systems in brownfield redevelopment is through education and outreach. By educating community members about the benefits of local food systems and involving them in the process, we can increase awareness and support for these initiatives. This can also lead to increased participation in community gardens and other food production sites, creating a sense of community and promoting healthy eating habits.



In addition to education and outreach, community engagement can also play a role in addressing issues of food insecurity. By involving community members in the planning and implementation of food systems, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of those who are most affected by food insecurity are taken into account. This can lead to more effective and sustainable solutions that address the root causes of food insecurity.



#### 18.3b Case Studies in Community Engagement and Food Systems



To further illustrate the importance of community engagement in food systems and brownfield redevelopment, let's take a look at some case studies.



One example is the Activating Change Together for Community Food Security (ACT for CFS) project in Nova Scotia, Canada. This project utilized PAR to better understand and improve community food security in the region. By involving community members in the research process, the project was able to identify key issues and develop effective solutions that were tailored to the specific needs of the community. The final reports from ACT for CFS can be accessed at http://foodarc.ca/project-pages/results-publications/, showcasing the success of community engagement in addressing food insecurity.



Another case study is the City of Baltimore's Vacants to Value program, which aims to revitalize vacant and abandoned properties in the city. As part of this program, the city has implemented community gardens and urban farms on these vacant lots, providing fresh produce to residents in food insecure neighborhoods. The success of this program can be attributed to the strong community engagement and involvement in the planning and implementation process.



#### 18.3c Challenges and Solutions in Community Engagement and Food Systems



While community engagement is crucial in promoting and sustaining food systems in brownfield redevelopment, there are also challenges that must be addressed. One challenge is ensuring that all community members have equal access and opportunity to participate in the process. This can be addressed by actively reaching out to marginalized and underrepresented groups and providing resources and support for their involvement.



Another challenge is maintaining long-term community engagement and involvement. This can be addressed by creating opportunities for ongoing education and collaboration, as well as involving community members in decision-making processes.



In conclusion, community engagement plays a vital role in the success of food systems in brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the planning and implementation process, we can ensure that the needs and preferences of the community are taken into account, leading to more effective and sustainable solutions. Through participatory action research, education and outreach, and addressing issues of food insecurity, community engagement can empower individuals and communities to achieve social change and improve food systems in brownfield redevelopment projects.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we explored the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and food systems. We learned about the potential benefits and challenges of redeveloping contaminated land for agricultural use, as well as the various strategies and policies that can be implemented to ensure the safety and sustainability of these projects. We also discussed the importance of community engagement and collaboration in brownfield redevelopment, particularly when it comes to addressing food insecurity and promoting equitable access to healthy food options.



As we continue to face the challenges of climate change and urbanization, brownfield redevelopment presents a unique opportunity to not only revitalize contaminated land, but also to create more resilient and sustainable food systems. By incorporating principles of environmental management and sustainable agriculture, we can transform once-blighted areas into thriving hubs of food production and distribution. However, it is crucial that we approach these projects with caution and consideration for the potential risks and impacts on both human health and the environment.



In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment and food systems are intricately linked and have the potential to bring about positive change in our communities. By working together and utilizing innovative approaches, we can create a more sustainable and equitable future for all.



### Exercises

Research and analyze a case study of a successful brownfield redevelopment project that incorporates sustainable food systems. Discuss the strategies and policies that were implemented and the outcomes of the project.



#### Exercise 2

Create a proposal for a brownfield redevelopment project that incorporates sustainable food systems. Consider the location, potential challenges, and strategies for community engagement and collaboration.



#### Exercise 3

Discuss the potential environmental and health risks associated with redeveloping contaminated land for agricultural use. How can these risks be mitigated and managed?



#### Exercise 4

Explore the concept of food sovereignty and its relationship to brownfield redevelopment. How can incorporating principles of food sovereignty benefit both the environment and the community?



#### Exercise 5

Interview a local community member or organization involved in a brownfield redevelopment project that incorporates sustainable food systems. Discuss their motivations, challenges, and successes in implementing the project.





## Chapter: Brownfield Redevelopment and Housing



### Introduction:



In this chapter, we will be discussing the topic of brownfield redevelopment and its relationship with housing. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances, pollutants, or other contaminants. These properties are often located in urban areas and can pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities. Brownfield redevelopment is the process of revitalizing these properties for new use, such as housing, in a safe and sustainable manner.



The redevelopment of brownfields can have a significant impact on the housing market. By repurposing these properties, developers can create new housing options in areas that may have been previously overlooked. This can help to alleviate housing shortages and increase the availability of affordable housing in urban areas. Additionally, the redevelopment of brownfields can also lead to economic benefits, such as job creation and increased property values.



However, the redevelopment of brownfields also presents unique challenges. The presence of contaminants on these properties requires careful planning and management to ensure the safety of future residents. This chapter will explore the various strategies and techniques used in brownfield redevelopment to mitigate environmental risks and create sustainable housing options. We will also discuss the role of government regulations and incentives in promoting brownfield redevelopment and housing. 





### Section: 19.1 Housing and Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in the field of environmental management, as it presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns. In this section, we will explore the relationship between housing and brownfields, and how the redevelopment of these properties can have a positive impact on the housing market.



#### 19.1a Definition of Housing



Before delving into the specifics of brownfield redevelopment and housing, it is important to define what we mean by "housing". Housing, or more generally, living spaces, refers to the construction and assigned usage of houses or buildings individually or collectively, for the purpose of shelter. This includes a range of options from apartments and houses to temporary shelters and emergency accommodations. Access to safe, affordable, and stable housing is essential for a person's health, safety, and well-being.



Housing also plays a critical role in shaping the quality of life for individuals, families, and communities. It can impact a person's economic, social, and cultural opportunities, as it influences their access to education, employment, healthcare, and social networks. In many countries, housing policies and programs have been developed to address issues related to affordability, quality, and availability, and to ensure that everyone has access to decent housing.



#### 19.1b Brownfield Redevelopment and Housing



Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances, pollutants, or other contaminants. These properties are often located in urban areas and can pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities. The redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns.



By repurposing these properties, developers can create new housing options in areas that may have been previously overlooked. This can help to alleviate housing shortages and increase the availability of affordable housing in urban areas. Additionally, the redevelopment of brownfields can also lead to economic benefits, such as job creation and increased property values.



However, the redevelopment of brownfields also presents unique challenges. The presence of contaminants on these properties requires careful planning and management to ensure the safety of future residents. This is where the field of environmental management comes into play.



#### 19.1c Environmental Management and Brownfield Redevelopment



Environmental management is the process of managing the impact of human activities on the environment. In the context of brownfield redevelopment, environmental management plays a crucial role in ensuring that these properties are safely and sustainably repurposed for housing.



One of the key strategies used in brownfield redevelopment is remediation, which involves the removal or treatment of contaminants on the property. This is done to ensure that the site is safe for future residents and to prevent any potential environmental hazards. Remediation can be a complex and costly process, but it is essential for the success of brownfield redevelopment projects.



In addition to remediation, environmental management also involves careful planning and monitoring throughout the redevelopment process. This includes conducting environmental assessments, developing risk management plans, and implementing sustainable practices to minimize the environmental impact of the redevelopment.



#### 19.1d Government Regulations and Incentives



The government also plays a crucial role in promoting brownfield redevelopment and housing. In many countries, there are regulations in place to ensure that brownfield redevelopment projects adhere to environmental standards and guidelines. These regulations help to protect the health and safety of future residents and the surrounding environment.



In addition to regulations, governments also offer incentives to encourage developers to take on brownfield redevelopment projects. These incentives can include tax breaks, grants, and other financial incentives to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment. By providing these incentives, governments can help to make brownfield redevelopment a more financially viable option for developers.



### Conclusion:



In conclusion, the redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns. By repurposing these properties, developers can create new housing options in urban areas, while also mitigating environmental risks. However, this process requires careful planning and management, as well as government support in the form of regulations and incentives. With proper environmental management practices and government support, brownfield redevelopment can be a successful and sustainable solution for both housing and environmental concerns.





### Section: 19.1 Housing and Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in the field of environmental management, as it presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns. In this section, we will explore the relationship between housing and brownfields, and how the redevelopment of these properties can have a positive impact on the housing market.



#### 19.1a Definition of Housing



Before delving into the specifics of brownfield redevelopment and housing, it is important to define what we mean by "housing". This includes a range of options from apartments and houses to temporary shelters and emergency accommodations. Housing also plays a critical role in shaping the quality of life for individuals, families, and communities. It can impact a person's economic, social, and cultural opportunities, as it influences their access to education, employment, healthcare, and social networks. In many countries, housing policies and programs have been developed to address issues related to affordability, quality, and availability, and to ensure that everyone has access to decent housing.



#### 19.1b Brownfield Redevelopment and Housing



Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances, pollutants, or other contaminants. These properties are often located in urban areas and can pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities. The redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns.



By repurposing these properties, developers can create new housing options in areas that may have been previously overlooked due to contamination concerns. This not only increases the availability of housing, but also helps to revitalize and improve the overall quality of the community. Additionally, the redevelopment of brownfields can also lead to job creation and economic growth in the area.



However, it is important to note that the redevelopment of brownfields must be done carefully and with consideration for the potential environmental impacts. Proper remediation and cleanup of the contaminated site must be conducted to ensure the safety and well-being of future residents. This can be a costly and time-consuming process, but the benefits to both the environment and the community make it a worthwhile investment.



In order to facilitate the redevelopment of brownfields, the Small Business Liability Relief and Brownfields Revitalization Act was passed. This act provides funding for brownfields assessment, cleanup, and job training programs, as well as promoting public-private partnerships to turn these properties into viable economic developments. By addressing both environmental and housing concerns, the redevelopment of brownfields can have a positive impact on the community and create a more sustainable future.





### Section: 19.1 Housing and Brownfields:



Brownfield redevelopment has become an increasingly important topic in the field of environmental management, as it presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns. In this section, we will explore the relationship between housing and brownfields, and how the redevelopment of these properties can have a positive impact on the housing market.



#### 19.1a Definition of Housing



Before delving into the specifics of brownfield redevelopment and housing, it is important to define what we mean by "housing". Housing, or more generally, living spaces, refers to the construction and assigned usage of houses or buildings individually or collectively, for the purpose of shelter. This includes a range of options from apartments and houses to temporary shelters and emergency accommodations. Access to safe, affordable, and stable housing is essential for a person's health, safety, and well-being.

In many countries, housing policies and programs have been developed to address issues related to affordability, quality, and availability, and to ensure that everyone has access to decent housing.



#### 19.1b Brownfield Redevelopment and Housing



Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that have been contaminated by hazardous substances, pollutants, or other contaminants. These properties are often located in urban areas and can pose significant health and environmental risks to nearby communities. The redevelopment of brownfields presents a unique opportunity to address both environmental and housing concerns.



By repurposing these properties, developers can create new housing options in areas that may have been previously overlooked due to contamination concerns. This not only increases the availability of housing, but also helps to revitalize and improve the surrounding community. Additionally, the use of existing buildings and materials in the adaptive building process can be more environmentally sustainable and cost-effective compared to building new structures.



#### 19.1c Case Studies in Housing and Brownfield Redevelopment



To further illustrate the positive impact of brownfield redevelopment on housing, let's take a look at some case studies. In the city of Baltimore, Maryland, the redevelopment of a former industrial site into a mixed-use development called Harbor Point has created over 1,000 new housing units, including affordable housing options. This project not only provided much-needed housing in the area, but also helped to clean up and revitalize a contaminated site.



In another example, the city of Portland, Oregon has implemented a brownfield redevelopment program that focuses on creating affordable housing options in areas with high levels of contamination. This program has successfully transformed several abandoned industrial sites into affordable housing developments, providing safe and stable housing for low-income residents.



These case studies demonstrate the potential for brownfield redevelopment to not only address environmental concerns, but also to improve the availability and quality of housing in communities. By utilizing existing buildings and materials, and working closely with local governments and communities, brownfield redevelopment can be a valuable tool in promoting sustainable and equitable housing options.





### Section: 19.2 Housing Strategies:



Housing strategies are essential for addressing the complex issues surrounding brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss various strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options in these areas.



#### 19.2a Overview of Housing Strategies



There are several key strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options. These include:



- Incentivizing developers: One of the most effective ways to encourage brownfield redevelopment is by providing incentives to developers. This can include tax breaks, grants, or other financial incentives to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment.

- Public-private partnerships: Collaborations between government agencies and private developers can also be effective in promoting brownfield redevelopment. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to overcome the challenges of redeveloping contaminated properties.

- Mixed-use development: Another strategy is to incorporate mixed-use development into brownfield redevelopment plans. This involves combining residential, commercial, and recreational spaces in a single development, which can help to create a more vibrant and sustainable community.

- Affordable housing initiatives: Brownfield redevelopment can also be used as an opportunity to address the issue of affordable housing. By including affordable housing units in redevelopment plans, developers can help to address the housing needs of low-income individuals and families.

- Green building practices: Incorporating green building practices into brownfield redevelopment can have multiple benefits. Not only does it help to reduce the environmental impact of the development, but it can also lead to cost savings for residents through energy-efficient design and construction.

- Community involvement: Engaging with the local community is crucial for successful brownfield redevelopment. By involving community members in the planning and decision-making process, developers can ensure that the redevelopment meets the needs and desires of the community.



These strategies can be used individually or in combination to promote brownfield redevelopment and create new housing options. However, it is important to note that each brownfield site is unique and may require a tailored approach to address its specific challenges and opportunities.



In the next section, we will explore some specific examples of how these strategies have been used in brownfield redevelopment projects around the world. By understanding these case studies, we can gain valuable insights into the best practices for successful brownfield redevelopment and housing strategies.





### Section: 19.2 Housing Strategies:



Housing strategies are essential for addressing the complex issues surrounding brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss various strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options in these areas.



#### 19.2a Overview of Housing Strategies



There are several key strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options. These include:



- Incentivizing developers: One of the most effective ways to encourage brownfield redevelopment is by providing incentives to developers. This can include tax breaks, grants, or other financial incentives to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment.

- Public-private partnerships: Collaborations between government agencies and private developers can also be effective in promoting brownfield redevelopment. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to overcome the challenges of redeveloping contaminated properties.

- Mixed-use development: Another strategy is to incorporate mixed-use development into brownfield redevelopment plans. This involves combining residential, commercial, and recreational spaces in a single development, which can help to create a more vibrant and sustainable community.

- Affordable housing initiatives: Brownfield redevelopment can also be used as an opportunity to address the issue of affordable housing. By including affordable housing units in redevelopment plans, developers can help to address the housing needs of low-income individuals and families.

- Green building practices: Incorporating green building practices into brownfield redevelopment can have multiple benefits. Not only does it help to reduce the environmental impact of the development, but it can also lead to cost savings for residents through energy-efficient design and construction.

- Community involvement: Engaging with the local community is crucial for successful brownfield redevelopment. Community involvement can help to ensure that the needs and concerns of residents are taken into account during the planning and development process. This can also help to build support and acceptance for the project within the community.



#### 19.2b Selection of Housing Strategies



When considering which housing strategies to implement for brownfield redevelopment, it is important to take into account the specific needs and challenges of the site. Factors such as the level of contamination, location, and community demographics can all play a role in determining the most effective strategies. Additionally, it is important to consider the long-term sustainability and affordability of the housing options being proposed.



One approach to selecting housing strategies is to use a multi-criteria decision-making (MCDM) framework. This involves evaluating potential strategies based on a set of criteria, such as cost, environmental impact, and social equity. By using this framework, decision-makers can weigh the pros and cons of each strategy and select the most suitable options for the specific brownfield site.



Another important consideration when selecting housing strategies is the potential for synergies between different approaches. For example, incorporating green building practices into a mixed-use development can not only reduce the environmental impact of the project, but also create more affordable and sustainable housing options for residents.



In addition to considering the specific strategies to be implemented, it is also important to develop a comprehensive plan for managing and monitoring the housing development. This can include regular inspections and maintenance to ensure the long-term sustainability and safety of the housing units. It is also important to involve the community in this process to ensure their ongoing support and involvement in the redevelopment project.



In conclusion, the selection of housing strategies for brownfield redevelopment requires careful consideration of the site-specific factors and the potential for synergies between different approaches. By using a multi-criteria decision-making framework and involving the community in the planning and management process, we can create successful and sustainable housing options in brownfield areas.





### Section: 19.2 Housing Strategies:



Housing strategies are essential for addressing the complex issues surrounding brownfield redevelopment. In this section, we will discuss various strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options in these areas.



#### 19.2a Overview of Housing Strategies



There are several key strategies that can be used to promote the redevelopment of brownfields and create new housing options. These include:



- Incentivizing developers: One of the most effective ways to encourage brownfield redevelopment is by providing incentives to developers. This can include tax breaks, grants, or other financial incentives to offset the costs of remediation and redevelopment.

- Public-private partnerships: Collaborations between government agencies and private developers can also be effective in promoting brownfield redevelopment. By working together, these partnerships can leverage resources and expertise to overcome the challenges of redeveloping contaminated properties.

- Mixed-use development: Another strategy is to incorporate mixed-use development into brownfield redevelopment plans. This involves combining residential, commercial, and recreational spaces in a single development, which can help to create a more vibrant and sustainable community.

- Affordable housing initiatives: Brownfield redevelopment can also be used as an opportunity to address the issue of affordable housing. By including affordable housing units in redevelopment plans, developers can help to address the housing needs of low-income individuals and families.

- Green building practices: Incorporating green building practices into brownfield redevelopment can have multiple benefits. Not only does it help to reduce the environmental impact of the development, but it can also lead to cost savings for residents through energy-efficient design and construction.

- Community involvement: Engaging with the local community is crucial in brownfield redevelopment, especially when it comes to housing strategies. Community involvement can help to ensure that the redevelopment plans align with the needs and desires of the community, and can also help to build support and trust for the project.



#### 19.2b Incentivizing Developers



Incentivizing developers is a key strategy for promoting brownfield redevelopment. Developers are often deterred from redeveloping brownfields due to the high costs associated with remediation and redevelopment. By providing financial incentives, such as tax breaks or grants, developers can be encouraged to take on these projects. This not only benefits the developers, but also the community by creating new housing options and revitalizing blighted areas.



#### 19.2c Public-Private Partnerships



Public-private partnerships can also be effective in promoting brownfield redevelopment. By working together, government agencies and private developers can leverage resources and expertise to overcome the challenges of redeveloping contaminated properties. These partnerships can also help to share the risks and costs associated with brownfield redevelopment, making it a more feasible option for developers.



#### 19.2d Mixed-Use Development



Incorporating mixed-use development into brownfield redevelopment plans can have numerous benefits. By combining residential, commercial, and recreational spaces in a single development, a more vibrant and sustainable community can be created. This can also help to attract a diverse range of residents and businesses, making the area more economically viable.



#### 19.2e Affordable Housing Initiatives



Brownfield redevelopment can also be used as an opportunity to address the issue of affordable housing. By including affordable housing units in redevelopment plans, developers can help to address the housing needs of low-income individuals and families. This can also help to promote diversity and inclusivity in the community.



#### 19.2f Green Building Practices



Incorporating green building practices into brownfield redevelopment can have multiple benefits. Not only does it help to reduce the environmental impact of the development, but it can also lead to cost savings for residents through energy-efficient design and construction. This can also help to promote sustainability and resilience in the community.



#### 19.2g Case Studies in Housing Strategies



To further illustrate the effectiveness of housing strategies in brownfield redevelopment, let's look at some case studies. One notable example is the Stamford Brook project, where 700 dwellings were built to high efficiency standards. The results of this project showed a significant gap between the expected energy use before construction and the actual energy use once the houses were occupied. This was largely due to workmanship issues, such as thermal bridges and internal partitions, which were not considered in the initial calculations.



Another case study is the work of Hopfe, which looked into uncertainties in building design, including workmanship. This study showed that the uncertainty in the value used for infiltration has the largest influence on cooling and heating demand. This highlights the importance of considering workmanship in housing strategies for brownfield redevelopment.



In conclusion, housing strategies play a crucial role in promoting brownfield redevelopment and creating new housing options. By incentivizing developers, forming public-private partnerships, incorporating mixed-use development, addressing affordable housing needs, and implementing green building practices, we can create more sustainable and inclusive communities while revitalizing contaminated areas. 





### Section: 19.3 Housing and Community Engagement:



Community engagement is a crucial aspect of brownfield redevelopment, particularly when it comes to housing. In this section, we will discuss the role of community engagement in promoting successful and sustainable housing developments on brownfield sites.



#### 19.3a Role of Community Engagement in Housing



Community empowerment and participation are key components of successful mixed-income housing developments. As Fraser and Nelson suggest, community empowerment is essential for fostering positive neighborhood relations, identifying community assets and needs, and maximizing the "neighborhood effects" of new developments. This is especially important in the context of brownfield redevelopment, where the community may have concerns about potential environmental hazards and the impact of new housing on the neighborhood.



One way to promote community engagement in housing developments is through the creation of central, shared community spaces with interesting programming. This can provide opportunities for diverse residents to mingle and socialize, fostering a sense of community and promoting social cohesion. Additionally, involving lower-income residents in the management and maintenance of their developments can help to empower them and give them a sense of ownership over their living space.



However, community engagement should not be limited to just physical integration and socialization. As Duke suggests, it is also important to ensure that marginalized groups have a voice in the decision-making process and the ability to effect change in their community. This is not only crucial for promoting successful integration, but it also upholds the fundamental right to the city for all residents.



In addition to promoting community empowerment, community engagement can also play a role in poverty alleviation. As research has shown, economically diverse and integrated neighborhoods can support residents' opportunities and life chances. By involving lower-income residents in the redevelopment process and providing affordable housing options, brownfield redevelopment can help to address the issue of housing affordability and promote social and economic equity.



Overall, community engagement is a crucial aspect of successful and sustainable housing developments on brownfield sites. By empowering and involving the community, developers can create more vibrant and inclusive neighborhoods that benefit all residents. 





### Section: 19.3 Housing and Community Engagement:



Community engagement is a crucial aspect of brownfield redevelopment, particularly when it comes to housing. In this section, we will discuss the role of community engagement in promoting successful and sustainable housing developments on brownfield sites.



#### 19.3a Role of Community Engagement in Housing



Community empowerment and participation are key components of successful mixed-income housing developments. As Fraser and Nelson suggest, community empowerment is essential for fostering positive neighborhood relations, identifying community assets and needs, and maximizing the "neighborhood effects" of new developments. In addition to promoting community empowerment, community engagement can also play a role in poverty alleviation. As research has shown, economically diverse and integrated neighborhoods can support residents' opportunities and life chances. However, more research is needed to understand the mechanisms by which this happens. Joseph begins to examine this in the case of Chicago, and further qualitative research could examine dynamics of neighbor.



#### 19.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Housing



There are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in housing developments on brownfield sites. One effective technique is community organizing, which involves bringing together community members to identify their needs and concerns, and to develop strategies for addressing them. This can help to build trust and collaboration between residents and developers, and can also empower community members to have a say in the decision-making process.



Another technique is participatory design, which involves involving community members in the design and planning of the housing development. This can help to ensure that the development meets the needs and preferences of the community, and can also foster a sense of ownership and pride in the project.



Community engagement can also be fostered through community-based organizations (CBOs) and non-governmental organizations (NGOs). These organizations can serve as intermediaries between the community and developers, helping to facilitate communication and collaboration. They can also provide resources and support for community members to participate in the development process.



In addition, developers can use creative and interactive methods to engage the community, such as hosting community events, workshops, and focus groups. These methods can help to gather input and feedback from community members, and can also promote a sense of inclusivity and transparency in the development process.



Overall, community engagement is crucial for promoting successful and sustainable housing developments on brownfield sites. By involving community members in the decision-making process and empowering them to have a say in the development, developers can foster positive relationships and promote social cohesion within the community. This can ultimately lead to more successful and integrated mixed-income housing developments.





### Section: 19.3 Housing and Community Engagement:



Community engagement is a crucial aspect of brownfield redevelopment, particularly when it comes to housing. In this section, we will discuss the role of community engagement in promoting successful and sustainable housing developments on brownfield sites.



#### 19.3a Role of Community Engagement in Housing

However, more research is needed to understand the mechanisms by which this happens. Joseph begins to examine this in the case of Chicago, and further qualitative research could examine dynamics of neighbor.



#### 19.3b Case Studies in Community Engagement and Housing



To further illustrate the importance of community engagement in housing developments, let's look at some case studies.



One successful example is the redevelopment of the former Cabrini-Green public housing project in Chicago. The new mixed-income development, called Parkside of Old Town, was designed with input from the community and includes a mix of affordable and market-rate units. The development also includes community spaces and programming to promote social interaction and empowerment among residents.



Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Navy Yard in Philadelphia. The community was heavily involved in the planning process and advocated for the inclusion of affordable housing in the development. As a result, the Navy Yard now includes a mix of affordable and market-rate housing, as well as community spaces and programs.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of community engagement in promoting successful and sustainable housing developments. By involving the community in the planning and management process, developers can create developments that meet the needs and desires of the community, while also promoting social cohesion and empowerment among residents.



#### 19.3c Challenges and Solutions for Community Engagement in Housing



While community engagement is crucial for successful housing developments, there are also challenges that must be addressed. One challenge is ensuring that all residents, particularly those from lower-income backgrounds, have equal opportunities to participate in the decision-making process. This can be addressed by providing resources and support for marginalized groups to participate, such as translation services and childcare.



Another challenge is maintaining community engagement and empowerment after the initial development is complete. This can be addressed by creating ongoing opportunities for residents to be involved in the management and decision-making processes, as well as providing resources for community programming and socialization.



In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial aspect of brownfield redevelopment and housing. By involving the community in the planning and management process, developers can create successful and sustainable housing developments that promote social cohesion, empowerment, and poverty alleviation. However, challenges must be addressed to ensure that all residents have equal opportunities to participate and that community engagement is maintained in the long term.





### Conclusion

In this chapter, we explored the important topic of brownfield redevelopment and its impact on housing. We learned about the definition of brownfields and the challenges they pose to the environment and public health. We also discussed the benefits of brownfield redevelopment, such as revitalizing communities and creating new housing opportunities. Additionally, we examined the various stakeholders involved in the redevelopment process and the importance of collaboration and communication among them.



One key takeaway from this chapter is the importance of environmental management in brownfield redevelopment. By implementing effective environmental management practices, we can ensure that the redevelopment process is carried out in a safe and sustainable manner. This includes conducting thorough site assessments, properly disposing of hazardous materials, and implementing remediation strategies to mitigate any potential risks.



Another important aspect of brownfield redevelopment is its potential to address housing shortages and promote affordable housing. By redeveloping abandoned or contaminated sites, we can create new housing opportunities and revitalize communities. This can also help to reduce urban sprawl and promote more sustainable development.



In conclusion, brownfield redevelopment is a complex and multifaceted process that requires collaboration and effective environmental management. By addressing the challenges posed by brownfields and utilizing sustainable practices, we can create new housing opportunities and revitalize communities while also protecting the environment and public health.
