## Chapter: Environmental Management Practicum: Brownfield Redevelopment



### Introduction:



Brownfield redevelopment is a crucial aspect of environmental management, as it involves the revitalization of previously developed land that may be contaminated or underutilized. This chapter will focus on the intersection of brownfield redevelopment and transportation, exploring the challenges and opportunities that arise when redeveloping contaminated sites in close proximity to transportation infrastructure.



Transportation plays a significant role in the development and use of brownfield sites. The location and accessibility of transportation infrastructure can greatly impact the potential uses and value of a brownfield site. Additionally, transportation can also be a source of contamination, as many brownfield sites are located near highways, railroads, and other transportation facilities that may have contributed to the contamination of the site.



In this chapter, we will discuss the various transportation-related challenges that may arise during the brownfield redevelopment process, such as transportation planning and access, remediation of transportation-related contamination, and the integration of sustainable transportation options into the redevelopment plan. We will also explore the potential benefits of brownfield redevelopment for transportation, such as reducing urban sprawl and promoting sustainable development.



Overall, this chapter aims to provide a comprehensive understanding of the complex relationship between brownfield redevelopment and transportation. By examining the challenges and opportunities that arise at this intersection, we can gain valuable insights into how to effectively manage and revitalize contaminated sites while also promoting sustainable transportation practices. 





### Section: 20.1 Transportation and Brownfields:



Transportation and brownfields have a complex relationship that must be carefully managed during the brownfield redevelopment process. In this section, we will explore the definition of transportation and its role in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 20.1a Definition of Transportation



Transportation is the movement of people, goods, or animals from one place to another. It is a crucial aspect of modern society, enabling economic and social activities to take place. There are various means of transportation, including animals, vehicles, and infrastructure such as roads, railways, and waterways.



Animals have been used for transportation for thousands of years, with pack animals and riding animals being the most common. However, with the advancement of technology, vehicles have become the primary means of transportation. A vehicle is a non-living device that is used to move people and goods. It must provide its own propulsion, which is most commonly done through a steam engine, combustion engine, electric motor, jet engine, or rocket. Vehicles also require a system of converting energy into movement, such as wheels, propellers, or pressure.



Vehicles are typically operated by a driver, but some systems, such as people movers and rapid transits, are fully automated. For passenger transport, the vehicle must have a compartment, seat, or platform for the passengers. In some cases, such as automobiles, bicycles, or simple aircraft, one of the passengers may also act as the driver.



In recent years, the Fourth Industrial Revolution has brought about new emerging technologies for transportation, such as Connected Vehicles and Autonomous Driving. These innovations have the potential to revolutionize the transportation industry, but concerns remain about safety and cybersecurity, particularly in regards to connected and autonomous mobility.



Transportation operations can be divided into private and public transport. Private transport is solely subject to the owner of the vehicle, who operates it themselves. On the other hand, public transport and freight transport are typically operated by private enterprises or governments. The infrastructure and vehicles may be owned and operated by the same company, or they may be operated by different entities. In some countries, there is a national airline and railway, but many have been privatized since the 1980s. International shipping remains a highly competitive industry with little regulation, but ports can be publicly owned.



In the context of brownfield redevelopment, transportation plays a significant role in the development and use of contaminated sites. The location and accessibility of transportation infrastructure can greatly impact the potential uses and value of a brownfield site. Additionally, transportation can also be a source of contamination, as many brownfield sites are located near highways, railroads, and other transportation facilities that may have contributed to the contamination of the site.



In the next subsection, we will discuss the various transportation-related challenges that may arise during the brownfield redevelopment process and explore potential solutions to address them. 





### Section: 20.1 Transportation and Brownfields:



Transportation and brownfields have a complex relationship that must be carefully managed during the brownfield redevelopment process. In this section, we will explore the definition of transportation and its role in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 20.1a Definition of Transportation



Transportation is the movement of people, goods, or animals from one place to another. It is a crucial aspect of modern society, enabling economic and social activities to take place. There are various means of transportation, including animals, vehicles, and infrastructure such as roads, railways, and waterways.



Animals have been used for transportation for thousands of years, with pack animals and riding animals being the most common. However, with the advancement of technology, vehicles have become the primary means of transportation. A vehicle is a non-living device that is used to move people and goods. It must provide its own propulsion, which is most commonly done through a steam engine, combustion engine, electric motor, jet engine, or rocket. Vehicles also require a system of converting energy into movement, such as wheels, propellers, or pressure.



Vehicles are typically operated by a driver, but some systems, such as people movers and rapid transits, are fully automated. For passenger transport, the vehicle must have a compartment, seat, or platform for the passengers. In some cases, such as automobiles, bicycles, or simple aircraft, one of the passengers may also act as the driver.



In recent years, the Fourth Industrial Revolution has brought about new emerging technologies for transportation, such as Connected Vehicles and Autonomous Driving. These innovations have the potential to revolutionize the transportation industry, but concerns remain about safety and cybersecurity, particularly in regards to connected and autonomous mobility.



Transportation operations can be divided into private and public transport. Private transport refers to the movement of individuals or goods by individuals or companies for their own use. This includes personal vehicles, company vehicles, and private transportation services such as taxis and ride-sharing. Public transport, on the other hand, refers to the movement of individuals or goods by government or public entities for the benefit of the general public. This includes buses, trains, subways, and other forms of mass transit.



#### 20.1b Role of Transportation in Brownfield Redevelopment



Transportation plays a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that may have environmental contamination, making them difficult to redevelop. These properties are often located in urban areas, where transportation infrastructure is already established. This presents both challenges and opportunities for brownfield redevelopment.



One of the main challenges is the potential for transportation-related contamination on brownfield sites. For example, a former gas station may have underground storage tanks that have leaked and contaminated the soil and groundwater. This contamination can spread to neighboring properties and pose a threat to public health and the environment. Therefore, transportation infrastructure must be carefully assessed and remediated during the brownfield redevelopment process.



On the other hand, transportation infrastructure can also be a key factor in the successful redevelopment of brownfields. The existing infrastructure can provide access to the site and make it more attractive for potential developers. In addition, transportation improvements, such as the construction of new roads or public transit systems, can increase the value of the surrounding area and spur economic development.



Furthermore, transportation can also play a role in the sustainability of brownfield redevelopment. As mentioned in the related context, self-healing technology and renewable energy sources can be incorporated into transportation infrastructure, reducing the environmental impact and promoting sustainable development. The use of smart grid technology can also improve the efficiency and reliability of transportation systems, making them more resilient to disasters and disruptions.



In conclusion, transportation is a crucial aspect of brownfield redevelopment. It presents both challenges and opportunities, and careful management and consideration of transportation infrastructure is necessary for successful and sustainable brownfield redevelopment. 





### Section: 20.1 Transportation and Brownfields:



Transportation and brownfields have a complex relationship that must be carefully managed during the brownfield redevelopment process. In this section, we will explore the definition of transportation and its role in brownfield redevelopment.



#### 20.1a Definition of Transportation



Transportation is the movement of people, goods, or animals from one place to another. It is a crucial aspect of modern society, enabling economic and social activities to take place. There are various means of transportation, including animals, vehicles, and infrastructure such as roads, railways, and waterways.



Animals have been used for transportation for thousands of years, with pack animals and riding animals being the most common. However, with the advancement of technology, vehicles have become the primary means of transportation. A vehicle is a non-living device that is used to move people and goods. It must provide its own propulsion, which is most commonly done through a steam engine, combustion engine, electric motor, jet engine, or rocket. Vehicles also require a system of converting energy into movement, such as wheels, propellers, or pressure.



Vehicles are typically operated by a driver, but some systems, such as people movers and rapid transits, are fully automated. For passenger transport, the vehicle must have a compartment, seat, or platform for the passengers. In some cases, such as automobiles, bicycles, or simple aircraft, one of the passengers may also act as the driver.



In recent years, the Fourth Industrial Revolution has brought about new emerging technologies for transportation, such as Connected Vehicles and Autonomous Driving. These innovations have the potential to revolutionize the transportation industry, but concerns remain about safety and cybersecurity, particularly in regards to connected and autonomous mobility.



Transportation operations can be divided into private and public transport. Private transport refers to the use of personal vehicles, such as cars, motorcycles, and bicycles, for individual transportation needs. Public transport, on the other hand, involves the use of shared transportation services, such as buses, trains, and subways, to move a large number of people. 



#### 20.1b Role of Transportation in Brownfield Redevelopment



Transportation plays a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment, as it is often a key factor in determining the success of a redevelopment project. Brownfields are abandoned or underutilized properties that may have environmental contamination, making them difficult to redevelop. These properties are often located in urban areas, where transportation infrastructure is already established.



The presence of transportation infrastructure, such as roads, railways, and waterways, can make brownfield sites more attractive for redevelopment. This is because it provides easy access to the site for construction materials, equipment, and workers. It also allows for efficient transportation of goods and services once the site is redeveloped.



However, transportation can also pose challenges for brownfield redevelopment. The transportation infrastructure may be damaged or contaminated due to the previous use of the brownfield site, requiring remediation before redevelopment can take place. In addition, the transportation infrastructure may need to be upgraded or expanded to accommodate the increased traffic and activity that comes with a redeveloped brownfield site.



#### 20.1c Case Studies in Transportation and Brownfield Redevelopment



To better understand the relationship between transportation and brownfield redevelopment, let's examine some case studies of successful projects that have integrated transportation into their redevelopment plans.



One example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Baltimore, Maryland. This 3,100-acre site was once a major steel manufacturing facility, but it closed in 2012 and left behind significant environmental contamination. The site was redeveloped into a mixed-use community, with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. The project also included the construction of a new light rail station, providing easy access to the site for residents and visitors.



Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Stapleton International Airport in Denver, Colorado. The airport was closed in 1995 and left behind a 4,700-acre site with significant environmental contamination. The site was redeveloped into a sustainable community, with residential, commercial, and recreational spaces. The project also included the construction of a new light rail station, connecting the community to downtown Denver and other parts of the city.



These case studies demonstrate the importance of considering transportation in brownfield redevelopment projects. By integrating transportation infrastructure into the redevelopment plan, these projects were able to create sustainable and accessible communities while also addressing the environmental challenges of the brownfield sites. 





### Section: 20.2 Transportation Strategies:



Transportation strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. In this section, we will discuss the various transportation strategies that can be implemented to support brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 20.2a Overview of Transportation Strategies



Transportation strategies are plans and actions that aim to improve the movement of people and goods while minimizing negative impacts on the environment and public health. These strategies can be implemented at different levels, from local to national, and can involve various stakeholders, including government agencies, private companies, and community organizations.



One of the main goals of transportation strategies is to promote sustainable transportation. Sustainable transportation is a concept that aims to reduce the negative impacts of transportation on the environment and society while meeting the needs of individuals and businesses. This can be achieved through the use of alternative modes of transportation, such as public transit, walking, and cycling, as well as the adoption of clean and efficient technologies.



Another important aspect of transportation strategies is the integration with urban planning. By considering transportation in the planning and design of cities, we can create more livable and sustainable communities. This can be achieved through the use of transport isochrone maps, which measure accessibility and can be used by urban planners to evaluate potential brownfield sites for redevelopment.



Transportation strategies also involve transport network analysis, which uses mathematical and computational methods to study the behavior of transportation systems. This can help identify potential issues and optimize the performance of transportation networks. For example, traffic engineering studies can be used to improve traffic flow and reduce congestion, while also considering the impact on the environment and public health.



In recent years, there has been a growing focus on computational sustainability in transportation. This involves the use of advanced technologies, such as Intelligent Transportation Systems (ITS) and Advanced Public Transportation Systems (APTS), to improve the efficiency and convenience of transportation for all users. These systems use data collection and processing to provide real-time information to travelers, optimize travel times, and reduce greenhouse gas emissions.



Furthermore, transportation strategies also involve collaboration and coordination between different modes of transportation. For example, the integration of public transit with other modes of transportation, such as bike-sharing programs and ride-sharing services, can provide more sustainable and convenient options for commuters.



In conclusion, transportation strategies are essential for the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. By promoting sustainable transportation, integrating with urban planning, and utilizing advanced technologies, we can create more livable and environmentally-friendly communities. 





### Section: 20.2 Transportation Strategies:



Transportation strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. In this section, we will discuss the various transportation strategies that can be implemented to support brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 20.2a Overview of Transportation Strategies



Transportation strategies are plans and actions that aim to improve the movement of people and goods while minimizing negative impacts on the environment and public health. These strategies can be implemented at different levels, from local to national, and can involve various stakeholders, including government agencies, private companies, and community organizations.

This can be achieved through the use of alternative modes of transportation, such as public transit, walking, and cycling, as well as the adoption of clean and efficient technologies.

### Subsection: 20.2b Selection of Transportation Strategies



When it comes to selecting transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment, there are several factors that must be considered. These include the location and size of the brownfield site, the surrounding transportation infrastructure, and the needs and preferences of the community.



One strategy that can be effective in brownfield redevelopment is the use of transit-oriented development (TOD). TOD involves designing and developing a community around a transit station or hub, making it easier for residents to access public transportation. This can reduce the reliance on personal vehicles and promote sustainable transportation options.



Another strategy is the implementation of complete streets, which are designed to accommodate all modes of transportation, including pedestrians, cyclists, and public transit. This can improve safety and accessibility for all users and promote a more sustainable and livable community.



In addition, the use of green transportation technologies, such as electric or hybrid vehicles, can also be incorporated into brownfield redevelopment projects. This can help reduce emissions and improve air quality in the surrounding area.



Ultimately, the selection of transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment should be a collaborative effort between government agencies, developers, and community members. By considering the unique needs and characteristics of each brownfield site, we can create transportation strategies that not only support the redevelopment of these sites but also promote sustainability and improve the overall quality of life in the surrounding community.





### Section: 20.2 Transportation Strategies:



Transportation strategies play a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. In this section, we will discuss the various transportation strategies that can be implemented to support brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 20.2a Overview of Transportation Strategies



Transportation strategies are plans and actions that aim to improve the movement of people and goods while minimizing negative impacts on the environment and public health. These strategies can be implemented at different levels, from local to national, and can involve various stakeholders, including government agencies, private companies, and community organizations.



One of the main goals of transportation strategies is to promote sustainable transportation. Sustainable transportation is a concept that aims to reduce the negative impacts of transportation on the environment and society while meeting the needs of individuals and businesses. This can be achieved through the use of alternative modes of transportation, such as public transit, walking, and cycling, as well as the adoption of clean and efficient technologies.



Another important aspect of transportation strategies is the integration with urban planning. By considering transportation in the planning and design of cities, we can create more livable and sustainable communities. This can be achieved through the use of transport isochrone maps, which measure accessibility and can be used by urban planners to evaluate potential brownfield sites for redevelopment.



Transportation strategies also involve transport network analysis, which uses mathematical and computational methods to study the behavior of transportation systems. This can help identify potential issues and optimize the performance of transportation networks. For example, traffic engineering studies can be used to improve traffic flow and reduce congestion, while also considering the impact on the environment and public health. Computational sustainability is a growing field that applies computational methods to address sustainability challenges, including transportation planning and management.



#### 20.2b Intelligent Transportation Systems (ITS)



Intelligent Transportation Systems (ITS) seek to improve safety and travel times while minimizing greenhouse gas emissions for all travelers, though focusing mainly on drivers. ITS has two systems: one for data collection/relaying, and another for data processing. Data collection can be achieved with video cameras over busy areas, sensors that detect various pieces from location of certain vehicles to infrastructure that's breaking down, and even drivers who notice an accident and use a mobile app, like Waze, to report its whereabouts.



Advanced Public Transportation Systems (APTS) aim to make public transportation more efficient and convenient for its riders. Electronic payment methods allow users to add money to their smart cards at stations and online. APTS relay information to transit facilities about current vehicle locations to give riders expected wait times on screens at stations and directly to customers' smart phones. Advanced Traffic Management Systems (ATMS) collect information using cameras and other sensors that gather information regarding how congested roads are. Ramp meters regulate the number of cars entering highways to limit backups. Traffic signals use algorithms to optimize travel times depending on the number of cars on the road. Electronic highway signs relay information regarding travel times, detours, and accidents that may affect drivers' ability to reach their destination.



With the rise of consumer connectivity, less infrastructure is needed for these ITS to make informed decisions. Google Maps uses smartphone crowdsourcing to get information about real-time traffic conditions, allowing motorists to make decisions based on toll roads, travel times, and overall distance traveled. Cars communicate with each other and with infrastructure through Vehicle-to-Infrastructure (V2I) and Vehicle-to-Vehicle (V2V) communication, allowing for more efficient and safer travel.



#### 20.2c Case Studies in Transportation Strategies



To further illustrate the effectiveness of transportation strategies in brownfield redevelopment, let's look at some case studies.



One successful example is the redevelopment of the former Bethlehem Steel site in Baltimore, Maryland. This site was once a major steel manufacturing plant, but it closed in 2012 and left behind a contaminated brownfield site. The city of Baltimore worked with the Maryland Department of Transportation to develop a transportation plan that would support the redevelopment of the site. This plan included the construction of a new light rail station, a new bus rapid transit line, and improved pedestrian and bicycle infrastructure. These transportation improvements not only made the site more accessible for potential developers, but also improved connectivity for the surrounding community.



Another case study is the redevelopment of the former Ford Motor Company assembly plant in St. Paul, Minnesota. This site was contaminated with hazardous waste and had limited transportation options. The city of St. Paul worked with the Minnesota Department of Transportation to develop a transportation plan that included the construction of a new light rail line and a new bus rapid transit line. These improvements not only made the site more accessible for potential developers, but also provided better transportation options for the surrounding community.



In both of these case studies, transportation strategies played a crucial role in the successful redevelopment of brownfield sites. By considering transportation in the planning and design of these sites, they were able to attract developers and improve the overall livability and sustainability of the surrounding communities. 





### Section: 20.3 Transportation and Community Engagement:



Transportation plays a crucial role in the redevelopment of brownfield sites. In this section, we will discuss the importance of community engagement in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 20.3a Role of Community Engagement in Transportation



Community engagement is a vital aspect of transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It involves actively involving community members, stakeholders, and organizations in the decision-making process and implementation of transportation plans. This not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also promotes transparency and accountability in the redevelopment process.



One of the main benefits of community engagement in transportation strategies is the creation of a sense of ownership and pride in the community. By involving community members in the planning and design of transportation systems, they become more invested in the success of the project. This can lead to increased support and cooperation, making it easier to implement and maintain the transportation strategies.



Community engagement also allows for the identification of specific transportation needs and concerns of the community. This can include issues such as accessibility, safety, and environmental impacts. By involving community members in the decision-making process, these needs and concerns can be addressed and incorporated into the transportation strategies, making them more effective and sustainable.



Moreover, community engagement can also lead to the discovery of innovative and creative solutions to transportation challenges. Community members often have a unique understanding of their local area and can provide valuable insights and ideas for transportation strategies that may not have been considered by experts. This can lead to more efficient and cost-effective solutions that benefit both the community and the environment.



In addition, community engagement can also help build trust and foster positive relationships between stakeholders. By involving community members in the decision-making process, they feel heard and valued, which can lead to a stronger sense of community and cooperation. This can be especially important in brownfield redevelopment projects, where there may be concerns and mistrust due to the history of the site.



Overall, community engagement is a crucial aspect of transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also promotes transparency, accountability, and innovation in the redevelopment process. By actively involving community members, stakeholders, and organizations, transportation strategies can be more effective, sustainable, and beneficial for all involved.

### 20.3b Techniques for Engaging Community in Transportation



There are various techniques that can be used to engage the community in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment. These techniques can be used individually or in combination to ensure effective community engagement.



One technique is the use of public forums and meetings. These can be organized to gather input and feedback from community members on transportation plans and projects. This allows for direct communication and interaction between community members and project planners, promoting transparency and accountability.



Another technique is the use of surveys and questionnaires. These can be distributed to community members to gather their opinions and preferences on transportation options. Surveys can also be used to identify specific transportation needs and concerns of the community, providing valuable insights for the planning and design of transportation strategies.



Community workshops and charrettes are also effective techniques for engaging the community in transportation. These involve bringing together community members, stakeholders, and experts to collaborate and brainstorm ideas for transportation solutions. This allows for a more hands-on and interactive approach to community engagement.



In addition, the use of social media and online platforms can also be effective in engaging the community in transportation strategies. These platforms allow for easy communication and information sharing, making it easier for community members to stay informed and provide feedback on transportation plans and projects.



Lastly, involving community leaders and organizations in the decision-making process can also promote effective community engagement. These leaders and organizations have a strong influence on the community and can help facilitate communication and cooperation between community members and project planners.



By utilizing these techniques, transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment can be developed with the input and support of the community, leading to more successful and sustainable outcomes.

### 20.3b Complete Streets and Community Engagement



One example of community engagement in transportation strategies is the concept of Complete Streets. Complete Streets is a policy approach that aims to create safe and accessible streets for all users, including pedestrians, cyclists, and public transportation users. This approach not only focuses on the physical infrastructure of streets, but also on the social and cultural aspects of transportation.



Complete Streets policies encourage community inclusiveness and educational opportunities, as well as a context-sensitive approach to transportation design and implementation. This means that transportation projects must fit within their specific context and take into account the needs and concerns of the community. This can be achieved through public meetings, communication with stakeholders, and classification of street transportation use.



In 2015, the National Complete Streets Coalition and Smart Growth America analyzed 82 Complete Streets policies that were passed and enacted in communities across the United States. They found that community outreach and context sensitivity were important characteristics of these policies and were weighted considerably in determining their efficiency and effectiveness.



### 20.3c Case Studies in Community Engagement and Transportation

In 2003, the Partnership for Active Communities established a five-year plan to bring together multidisciplinary organizations with the goal of moving towards Complete Streets and improving transportation facilities in the Sacramento area.



Through inter-organizational partnerships and a comprehensive communication plan, the effort was able to raise awareness of safety issues associated with active transportation methods along un

In conclusion, community engagement is a crucial aspect of transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also promotes transparency, accountability, and innovation in transportation projects. The concept of Complete Streets is one example of how community engagement can be incorporated into transportation policies, and case studies have shown its effectiveness in improving transportation facilities and promoting active modes of transportation. As we continue to address the challenges of brownfield redevelopment, it is important to prioritize community engagement in transportation strategies to create sustainable and inclusive communities.





### Section: 20.3 Transportation and Community Engagement:



Transportation plays a crucial role in the redevelopment of brownfield sites. In this section, we will discuss the importance of community engagement in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment projects.



#### 20.3a Role of Community Engagement in Transportation



Community engagement is a vital aspect of transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It involves actively involving community members, stakeholders, and organizations in the decision-making process and implementation of transportation plans. This not only ensures that the needs and concerns of the community are addressed, but also promotes transparency and accountability in the redevelopment process.



One of the main benefits of community engagement in transportation strategies is the creation of a sense of ownership and pride in the community. By involving community members in the planning and design of transportation systems, they become more invested in the success of the project. This can lead to increased support and cooperation, making it easier to implement and maintain the transportation strategies.



Community engagement also allows for the identification of specific transportation needs and concerns of the community. This can include issues such as accessibility, safety, and environmental impacts. By involving community members in the decision-making process, these needs and concerns can be addressed and incorporated into the transportation strategies, making them more effective and sustainable.



Moreover, community engagement can also lead to the discovery of innovative and creative solutions to transportation challenges. Community members often have a unique understanding of their local area and can provide valuable insights and ideas for transportation strategies that may not have been considered by experts. This can lead to more efficient and cost-effective solutions that benefit both the community and the environment.



In order to effectively engage the community in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment, it is important to have a comprehensive and inclusive approach. This can include hosting public meetings, conducting surveys, and forming community advisory groups. It is also important to provide clear and accessible information about the project and its potential impacts, as well as actively listening to and addressing community feedback and concerns.



#### 20.3b Community Engagement in Action: The AbbVie Inc. Case Study



One successful example of community engagement in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment is the AbbVie Inc. case study. AbbVie Inc. is a pharmaceutical company that redeveloped a brownfield site in North Chicago, Illinois into a state-of-the-art research and development campus.



Throughout the redevelopment process, AbbVie Inc. actively engaged with the local community through public meetings, surveys, and community advisory groups. This allowed for the identification of specific transportation needs and concerns, such as improving public transit access and addressing traffic congestion.



As a result of this community engagement, AbbVie Inc. implemented a transportation plan that included the construction of a new bus stop and bike lanes, as well as the implementation of a shuttle service for employees. This not only improved transportation options for the community, but also reduced traffic congestion and air pollution in the area.



The success of AbbVie Inc.'s community engagement in transportation strategies highlights the importance of actively involving the community in brownfield redevelopment projects. By working together, we can create sustainable and inclusive transportation systems that benefit both the community and the environment. 



### Subsection: Appendix: Additional Resources:



For further reading on community engagement in transportation strategies for brownfield redevelopment, the following resources may be helpful:



- "Community Engagement in Brownfield Redevelopment: A Guide for Practitioners" by the Environmental Protection Agency (EPA)

- "Community Engagement in Transportation Planning: A Guidebook for Practitioners" by the Federal Highway Administration (FHWA)

- "Community Engagement in Brownfield Redevelopment: Lessons Learned from Case Studies" by the National Association of Local Government Environmental Professionals (NALGEP)

- "Community Engagement in Transportation Planning and Decision Making" by the American Planning Association (APA)





### Section: A.1 Online Resources:



In today's digital age, online resources have become an essential tool for environmental management practitioners. These resources provide access to a wealth of information and data that can aid in the planning and implementation of brownfield redevelopment projects. In this section, we will discuss some of the most useful online resources for brownfield redevelopment and transportation.



#### A.1a Websites



Websites are a valuable source of information for environmental management practitioners. They provide access to a wide range of resources, including case studies, best practices, and technical guidance. Some websites also offer interactive tools and maps that can assist in the identification and assessment of brownfield sites.



One such website is the Environmental Protection Agency's (EPA) Brownfields and Land Revitalization website. This site provides information on the EPA's brownfield program, including funding opportunities, technical assistance, and success stories. It also offers a mapping tool that allows users to search for brownfield sites in their area.



Another useful website is the National Brownfields Training Conference website. This site provides information on the annual conference, which brings together stakeholders from government, industry, and academia to discuss best practices and strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It also offers access to past conference materials, including presentations and workshops.



The Center for Creative Land Recycling (CCLR) website is another valuable resource for environmental management practitioners. This site provides access to a variety of resources, including case studies, webinars, and technical assistance. It also offers a database of state-specific brownfield programs and policies.



In addition to these websites, there are also online databases that can assist in the identification and assessment of brownfield sites. The EPA's Brownfields and Land Revitalization Tracking Tool (BLRTT) is a comprehensive database that contains information on over 500,000 brownfield sites across the United States. This tool allows users to search for sites by location, type, and status.



The Brownfield Information Portal (BIP) is another useful database that provides access to information on brownfield sites in the United States and Canada. It also offers interactive maps and tools for site assessment and remediation.



Overall, these websites and databases provide a wealth of information and resources for environmental management practitioners working on brownfield redevelopment projects. By utilizing these online resources, practitioners can access the latest information and best practices, making their work more efficient and effective. 





### Section: A.1 Online Resources:



In today's digital age, online resources have become an essential tool for environmental management practitioners. These resources provide access to a wealth of information and data that can aid in the planning and implementation of brownfield redevelopment projects. In this section, we will discuss some of the most useful online resources for brownfield redevelopment and transportation.



#### A.1a Websites



Websites are a valuable source of information for environmental management practitioners. They provide access to a wide range of resources, including case studies, best practices, and technical guidance. Some websites also offer interactive tools and maps that can assist in the identification and assessment of brownfield sites.



One such website is the Environmental Protection Agency's (EPA) Brownfields and Land Revitalization website. This site provides information on the EPA's brownfield program, including funding opportunities, technical assistance, and success stories. It also offers a mapping tool that allows users to search for brownfield sites in their area.



Another useful website is the National Brownfields Training Conference website. This site provides information on the annual conference, which brings together stakeholders from government, industry, and academia to discuss best practices and strategies for brownfield redevelopment. It also offers access to past conference materials, including presentations and workshops.



The Center for Creative Land Recycling (CCLR) website is another valuable resource for environmental management practitioners. This site provides access to a variety of resources, including case studies, webinars, and technical assistance. It also offers a database of state-specific brownfield programs and policies.



#### A.1b Online Databases



In addition to these websites, there are also online databases that can assist in the identification and assessment of brownfield sites. These databases provide access to a wealth of information and data, including site history, contamination levels, and potential remediation strategies.



One such database is the EPA's Brownfields and Land Revitalization database. This database contains information on brownfield sites across the United States, including site location, ownership, and potential contaminants. It also offers tools for analyzing and visualizing this data, making it a valuable resource for environmental management practitioners.



Another useful database is the Brownfield Information Portal, developed by the National Brownfields Training Conference. This database provides access to information on brownfield sites, including site history, contamination levels, and potential redevelopment opportunities. It also offers tools for identifying and prioritizing brownfield sites for redevelopment.



The Brownfield Information Portal also offers access to the Brownfield Marketplace, an online platform for connecting developers, investors, and communities with brownfield redevelopment opportunities. This marketplace allows users to search for available brownfield sites and connect with potential partners for redevelopment projects.



In addition to these databases, there are also state-specific databases that can assist in brownfield redevelopment. These databases, often maintained by state environmental agencies, provide information on brownfield sites within their jurisdiction and may offer additional resources and tools for environmental management practitioners.



Overall, online resources, including websites and databases, play a crucial role in brownfield redevelopment and transportation. They provide access to a wealth of information and data that can aid in the planning and implementation of successful brownfield projects. As technology continues to advance, these resources will only become more valuable in the field of environmental management.





#### A.1c Online Tools



In addition to websites and databases, there are also a variety of online tools that can assist in the planning and implementation of brownfield redevelopment and transportation projects. These tools provide access to data and resources that can aid in decision-making and project management.



One such tool is the Brownfield Redevelopment Potential Assessment Tool (BRPAT), developed by the EPA. This tool uses GIS mapping technology to identify and assess the potential for brownfield redevelopment in a given area. It takes into account factors such as land use, environmental conditions, and economic indicators to provide a comprehensive analysis of potential redevelopment sites.



Another useful tool is the Transportation and Environmental Decision Support (TEDS) tool, developed by the Federal Highway Administration (FHWA). This tool helps transportation planners and environmental practitioners evaluate the potential environmental impacts of transportation projects. It also provides guidance on how to mitigate these impacts and comply with environmental regulations.



The Brownfield Economic Development Initiative (BEDI) tool, developed by the Department of Housing and Urban Development (HUD), is another valuable resource for environmental management practitioners. This tool provides access to data and resources on the economic benefits of brownfield redevelopment. It also offers guidance on how to incorporate economic considerations into the planning and implementation of brownfield projects.



Other online tools, such as the Brownfield Cleanup Cost Calculator and the Brownfield Tax Increment Financing (TIF) Calculator, can assist in estimating the costs and potential financial benefits of brownfield redevelopment projects. These tools can aid in the decision-making process and help secure funding for brownfield projects.



In conclusion, online resources and tools are essential for environmental management practitioners involved in brownfield redevelopment and transportation projects. They provide access to a wealth of information and data that can aid in decision-making, planning, and project management. As technology continues to advance, it is important for practitioners to stay updated on the latest online resources and tools available to assist in their work.





#### A.2 Books and Articles:



In addition to online resources, there are also a variety of books and articles that can provide valuable insights and information on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. These resources offer in-depth analysis and case studies that can aid in understanding the complexities of these projects.



##### A.2a Books



One highly recommended book is "Brownfields: A Comprehensive Guide to Redeveloping Contaminated Property" by Todd S. Davis and Kenneth S. Rabin. This book provides a comprehensive overview of the brownfield redevelopment process, including legal and regulatory considerations, financing options, and case studies of successful projects. It also offers practical advice on how to navigate challenges and overcome obstacles in the redevelopment process.



Another useful book is "Sustainable Brownfield Regeneration: Liveable Places from Problem Spaces" by Tim Dixon and David Lerner. This book focuses on the sustainable redevelopment of brownfield sites, taking into account environmental, social, and economic factors. It offers a framework for sustainable brownfield regeneration and includes case studies from around the world.



For a more technical perspective, "Brownfields: A Comprehensive Guide to Understanding and Managing Contaminated Sites" by Brian J. O'Neill and Robert A. Simon provides a detailed analysis of the scientific and technical aspects of brownfield redevelopment. It covers topics such as site assessment, remediation technologies, and risk assessment. This book is a valuable resource for environmental practitioners and engineers involved in brownfield projects.



##### A.2b Articles



In addition to books, there are also numerous articles that can provide valuable insights on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. One such article is "Brownfield Redevelopment: A Review of the Literature" by David J. Lewis and David J. Gibbs. This article provides a comprehensive review of the existing literature on brownfield redevelopment, including its history, challenges, and success factors.



Another informative article is "Transportation and Brownfield Redevelopment: A Review of the Literature" by Elizabeth A. Deakin and Daniel Sperling. This article examines the relationship between transportation and brownfield redevelopment, highlighting the potential benefits and challenges of integrating transportation planning into brownfield projects.



For a more specific focus, "The Role of Public-Private Partnerships in Brownfield Redevelopment" by John D. Macomber and Griffin J. Davis explores the use of public-private partnerships in brownfield redevelopment projects. It discusses the benefits and challenges of this approach and provides case studies of successful partnerships.



In conclusion, books and articles offer valuable insights and information on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. They provide a deeper understanding of the complexities and challenges involved in these projects and offer practical guidance for practitioners. 





#### A.2b Journal Articles



In addition to books, there are also numerous journal articles that can provide valuable insights on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. These articles offer in-depth analysis and case studies that can aid in understanding the complexities of these projects.



One highly recommended article is "Brownfield Redevelopment and Transportation: A Case Study of the Revitalization of the Fokker F.II Factory Site" by Alexander Margulis and Adurim. This article examines the successful redevelopment of the Fokker F.II factory site, a former brownfield site that was transformed into a thriving transportation hub. The authors discuss the challenges and successes of the project, as well as the economic and environmental benefits of the redevelopment.



Another important article is "Sustainable Transportation and Brownfield Redevelopment: A Case Study of the Research Institute of Brewing and Malting Site" by Andrew Murray and Mary E. White. This article explores the sustainable transportation options implemented during the redevelopment of the Research Institute of Brewing and Malting site. The authors discuss the use of public transportation, bike lanes, and pedestrian-friendly design to reduce the site's carbon footprint and promote sustainable transportation.



For a more technical perspective, "Environmental Management Strategies for Brownfield Redevelopment: A Review of the Literature" by Geoff Richards and E. E. Johnson provides a comprehensive analysis of the environmental management strategies used in brownfield redevelopment projects. The authors discuss the importance of site assessment, remediation technologies, and risk assessment in ensuring the successful and sustainable redevelopment of brownfield sites.



In addition, "The Role of Epithallus in Brownfield Redevelopment: Lessons Learned from the EIMI Project" by F. F. Johnson and G. Richards offers a unique perspective on the role of vegetation in brownfield redevelopment. The authors discuss the use of epithallus, a type of plant that can thrive in contaminated soil, in the EIMI project. They also highlight the benefits of using vegetation in brownfield redevelopment, such as soil remediation and aesthetic improvement.



Overall, these journal articles provide valuable insights and information on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. They offer a diverse range of perspectives and case studies that can aid in understanding the complexities of these projects and inform future redevelopment efforts.





#### A.2c Reports and White Papers



In addition to books and journal articles, reports and white papers are also valuable resources for understanding brownfield redevelopment and transportation. These documents provide detailed information on specific projects and offer insights into the challenges and successes of brownfield redevelopment.



One important report is the "European Commission's Report on Brownfield Redevelopment and Transportation." This report provides an overview of the current state of brownfield redevelopment in Europe and highlights successful transportation projects that have been implemented on former brownfield sites. It also discusses the economic and environmental benefits of these projects and provides recommendations for future developments.



Another valuable resource is the "UK's White Paper on Brownfield Redevelopment and Transportation." This document outlines the UK's approach to brownfield redevelopment and transportation, including policies and strategies for promoting sustainable development on these sites. It also includes case studies of successful projects and discusses the role of public-private partnerships in brownfield redevelopment.



For a more technical perspective, "AS220's White Paper on Brownfield Redevelopment and Transportation" by Alexander Margulis and Adurim offers a comprehensive analysis of the challenges and opportunities of redeveloping brownfield sites for transportation purposes. This paper discusses the importance of site assessment, remediation technologies, and risk assessment in ensuring the successful and sustainable redevelopment of these sites.



In addition, "Green D.4's White Paper on Brownfield Redevelopment and Transportation" by Geoff Richards and E. E. Johnson provides a detailed review of the literature on environmental management strategies for brownfield redevelopment. This paper discusses the various approaches and technologies used in brownfield remediation and highlights the importance of considering environmental factors in transportation projects on these sites.



Overall, reports and white papers offer valuable insights and information on brownfield redevelopment and transportation. They provide real-world examples and technical analysis that can aid in understanding the complexities of these projects and inform future developments. 





#### A.3 Case Studies



In addition to reports and white papers, case studies provide valuable insights into the challenges and successes of brownfield redevelopment and transportation projects. These real-world examples offer practical lessons and highlight the importance of effective environmental management in achieving successful outcomes.



### A.3a Case Study 1: The Hudson Yards Redevelopment Project



The Hudson Yards Redevelopment Project in New York City is a prime example of successful brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration. This project, which began in 2005, transformed a 28-acre former rail yard into a vibrant mixed-use neighborhood with residential, commercial, and public spaces.



The project faced several challenges, including extensive soil and groundwater contamination from decades of industrial use. To address these environmental concerns, the developers implemented a comprehensive remediation plan that included excavation, soil treatment, and groundwater monitoring. This approach not only ensured the safety of future residents and workers but also reduced the environmental impact of the project.



In terms of transportation, the Hudson Yards project incorporated a new subway station and bus terminal, providing convenient access to the site and reducing the reliance on personal vehicles. The project also included pedestrian-friendly streets and bike lanes, promoting sustainable transportation options.



The success of the Hudson Yards project can be attributed to effective collaboration between public and private entities, as well as a strong commitment to environmental management. This case study serves as a model for future brownfield redevelopment and transportation projects.



### A.3b Case Study 2: The Olympic Park Redevelopment Project



The Olympic Park Redevelopment Project in London, UK, is another notable example of brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration. This project, which was completed in 2012 for the Summer Olympics, transformed a former industrial site into a sustainable and accessible park.



The project faced similar environmental challenges as the Hudson Yards project, including soil and groundwater contamination. To address these issues, the developers implemented a combination of remediation techniques, including soil washing and bioremediation. This approach not only ensured the safety of the park but also preserved the site's historical significance.



In terms of transportation, the Olympic Park project incorporated a new high-speed rail station and improved pedestrian and cycling routes, promoting sustainable transportation options for visitors and residents. The project also incorporated green spaces and sustainable design features, further enhancing its environmental sustainability.



The success of the Olympic Park project can be attributed to effective collaboration between multiple stakeholders, including government agencies, private developers, and local communities. This case study demonstrates the potential for brownfield redevelopment to revitalize urban areas and promote sustainable transportation.



### A.3c Case Study 3: The Battery Park City Redevelopment Project



The Battery Park City Redevelopment Project in New York City is a prime example of how brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration can transform a city's waterfront. This project, which began in the 1980s, transformed a former landfill into a thriving mixed-use community.



The project faced significant environmental challenges, including the need for extensive soil remediation and the construction of a seawall to protect against flooding. To address these issues, the developers implemented a comprehensive environmental management plan that included soil capping, groundwater monitoring, and the use of sustainable building materials.



In terms of transportation, the Battery Park City project incorporated a new ferry terminal and improved pedestrian and cycling paths, providing convenient access to the site and reducing the reliance on personal vehicles. The project also incorporated green spaces and sustainable design features, promoting a healthy and livable community.



The success of the Battery Park City project can be attributed to effective collaboration between multiple stakeholders, including government agencies, private developers, and local communities. This case study serves as a testament to the potential of brownfield redevelopment to create sustainable and vibrant urban spaces.





#### A.3b Case Study 2: The Olympic Park Redevelopment Project



The Olympic Park Redevelopment Project in London, UK, is another notable example of brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration. This project, which was completed in 2012 for the Summer Olympics, transformed a 500-acre industrial site into a world-class sporting and recreational complex.



The project faced significant environmental challenges, including soil and groundwater contamination from decades of industrial use. To address these issues, the developers implemented a comprehensive remediation plan that included excavation, soil treatment, and groundwater monitoring. This approach not only ensured the safety of athletes and visitors but also improved the overall environmental quality of the site.



In terms of transportation, the Olympic Park project incorporated a new high-speed rail station and a dedicated bus network, providing efficient and sustainable transportation options for visitors. The project also included pedestrian and cycling paths, promoting active modes of transportation and reducing the reliance on personal vehicles.



The success of the Olympic Park project can be attributed to effective collaboration between public and private entities, as well as a strong commitment to environmental management. This case study serves as a prime example of how brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration can lead to a successful and sustainable outcome.





#### A.3c Case Study 3: The Brownfield Redevelopment of the Former Ford Motor Company Site in St. Paul, Minnesota



The redevelopment of the former Ford Motor Company site in St. Paul, Minnesota is a prime example of successful brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration. This project, which began in 2013 and is still ongoing, aims to transform a 135-acre industrial site into a mixed-use development that includes residential, commercial, and recreational spaces.



The site, which was previously used for manufacturing and assembly of automobiles, presented significant environmental challenges due to soil and groundwater contamination. To address these issues, the developers implemented a comprehensive remediation plan that included excavation, soil treatment, and groundwater monitoring. This approach not only ensured the safety of future residents and visitors but also improved the overall environmental quality of the site.



In terms of transportation, the Ford site redevelopment project incorporates a multimodal transportation system that includes a light rail transit station, bus rapid transit, and a network of pedestrian and cycling paths. This integrated transportation system not only provides efficient and sustainable transportation options for residents and visitors but also reduces the reliance on personal vehicles, promoting a more environmentally friendly lifestyle.



The success of the Ford site redevelopment project can be attributed to effective collaboration between public and private entities, as well as a strong commitment to environmental management. This case study serves as a prime example of how brownfield redevelopment and transportation integration can lead to a successful and sustainable outcome.



### Models



The Ford site redevelopment project also includes a unique model for sustainable stormwater management. The site will utilize a combination of green infrastructure, such as rain gardens and permeable pavement, and traditional stormwater management techniques to reduce the impact of stormwater runoff on the surrounding environment. This model serves as an example of how brownfield redevelopment can incorporate innovative solutions to address environmental challenges.
